when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她的確做了一些 , 但真正的情況是 , 說未來會遠遠超過這個 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這傢伙出現了 , alanturing , 1936年 , 再次發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器完全是機械的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論上
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩位都是從數學的角度來的 , 但turing告訴我們一些非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 然後說: 「 不管你如何製造電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不論你電腦的機械性 , 像babbage一樣 , 或是電子 , 就像現在的電腦一樣 , 或是未來 , 細胞 , 或者 , 再一次 , 機械 , 一旦我們進入了奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 把它做得很小 。 所有這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上 , 計算本質上
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做 " 教堂 " 的論文 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	所以 , 突然間 , 你會看到這個連結 , 你說這個東西babbage已經建立了一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它有能力用電腦做所有事情 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓大家知道它有多慢 , 大約有1k的記憶 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它使用了打孔卡片 , 也就是被餵進去 , 它的速度大約是第一個zx81的一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一個拉姆包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以加上許多額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天這帶給我們哪裡呢 ?
so there are plans .	所以還有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典 , 科學博物館的檔案庫中 , 有數百個計劃和數千頁的筆記 , 是由查爾斯•巴貝奇所寫的 , 關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中有一組我們稱之為計畫28的計畫 , 這也是我和doronsoad一起開始的慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的運算員 , 也是驅動專案的人 , 來建造改變引擎 , 我們的計畫是建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南部這裡 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個計劃有幾個部分
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	一個是掃描babbage的檔案 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二個是關於所有這些計畫的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是那台機器的電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是要在科學博物館實體建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造出來時 , 你終於能夠了解一個電腦是如何運作的 , 因為與其在你面前有一個小小的晶片 , 你必須看著這個大小的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體操作 , 我看到cpu運作 , 我聽見它運作 , 我聽見它運作 。 我大概在聞它的味道 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫道 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎存在 , 它肯定會引導未來的科學發展 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有建造過它 , 因為他總是在忙著新計畫 , 但當它確實在1940年代建立 , 當然 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我給大家看一下它在動作時的樣子 , 它只顯示cpu機制的一部分在運作 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以這只是三組齒輪 , 還會加上這個 。 這是加入的機制 , 所以你想像一下這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年的時間 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代發生之前 , 我們就會有
thank you very much .	非常感謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個影像式的演講中 , yannarhustbertrand展現了他三個最近的項目 , 關於人類以及我們的棲息地 , 在他的系列中 , 驚人的空白照片-- " 來自地球 , " 來自全球的個人訪談 , 在他的網絡專案 " 60億 " 中 , 他在他的網頁中展示了他的三部最近項目 , " 家 " , 透過呼吸影片 , 記錄人類對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人性、媒體、攝影等 ,
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅南•阿斯伯特蘭在廣角度捕捉到脆弱的地球
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 要靠飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了九噸的二氧化碳 ; 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談談生態 , 我一年內排放出的二氧化碳和法國人一樣多 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我得要做什麼 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	我回家後必須殺一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來做我的碳定位 , 就像我每次做的事一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的作品是展現我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 是我去年拍的最後一張照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯塔沙油 , 很多污染
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 ; 我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達人工作非op , 24小時到7小時 , 盡可能多提煉石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的末端
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙並不是一個長期的解決方案
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油量比我們發現的還多三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的
coral reef in new caledonia .	新加利亞的珊瑚礁
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	百分之百的珊瑚可能在2050年之前就被消滅了 , 因為全球暖化 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	而且你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋生物多樣性非常重要 。
north pole . i've done this picture last summer .	北極 。 去年夏天我已經做了這張照片 。
it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前不可能做到這張照片 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	現在大西洋和太平洋之間有了新的方式 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	北極的厚度從1960年就減少了40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	沒有冰的吉利曼傑羅有新的面貌 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它失去了80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家 , 在一百年內 , 所有的山冰都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命非常重要 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像高爾告訴你的 , 有20億人住在喜馬拉雅冰河的水上 。
return of fish men .	返回魚男人 。
one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	五分之一的人類取決於魚類生存
today now 70 percent of the fish stock are overexploited .	現在有百分之七十的魚股過度利用了 。
according to fao , if we don't change our system of fishing the main sea resources will be gone in 2050 .	根據fao , 如果我們不改變我們捕撈主要海資源的系統 , 會在2050年消失 。

here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國這裡 , 90%的玉米培養是用來餵食動物或做石油 。

the name of the movie is " home " " maison . "	這部電影的名字是 「 家 」 ── 「 梅毒 」 。

these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 幾億年前
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	而我們人類已經直立行走了20萬年 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們已經成功地適應了 , 並且征服了整個地球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	數個世代以來 , 我們一直在養育孩子 , 不像其他數百萬的物種生活在我們身邊 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去30年來 , 我密切地看著地球和它的居民 , 從天上升起 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生活與地球的福祉息息相關 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚、繁殖、養殖 , 仍然是世界上最重要的人類佔領 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	而把我們結合在一起的 , 遠比我們分裂的事物還要偉大 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都有同樣的需求 , 對地球的禮物而言 , 同樣的願望能上升 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而我們卻帶著長城保持距離 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	今天我們最大的戰役是保護我們星球的自然提供 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	不到50年 , 我們徹底改變了它 , 比人類的整個歷史更為徹底 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林已經消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源的經費低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集耕作正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源不是永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們自己瀕臨絕種 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距越來越廣 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們尚未明白 , 我們要走的速度比地球維持得更快 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道現今的解決方案是可行的
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有能力去改變這個趨勢 。
so what are we waiting for ?	那我們在等什麼呢 ?

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在這場tedxboston的演講中 , 理查德•雷斯尼克在基因組定序時的便宜和快速基因定序即將把醫療照護顛倒 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、衛生保健、科學、科技、科技、
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•雷尼克:歡迎來到基因體革命
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向你們展示人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性別染色體
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大x染色體 ; 男性有x , 當然 , 還有y的小小複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	對不起男孩 , 但這只是個小東西 , 讓你不一樣 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以如果你放大這個基因組 , 那麼你看到的當然 , 就是這個雙螺旋結構--生命的編碼--拼出這四個生化字母 , 或者我們稱之為鹼基 , 沒錯:a , c , g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 30億
is that a big number ?	這是個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以隨意丟出大數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我在這個1280年的每一塊像素上放一個鹼基 , 到800個解析度螢幕上 , 我們需要3000個螢幕來檢視基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順便一提 , y染色體決定要將它定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以 , 15年後 , 大約40億美元後 , 基因組的序列和發表 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最後的版本被發表了 , 他們一直在努力 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這些都是在一個看起來像這樣子的機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每個鹼基的成本都很緩慢 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我在這裡告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	現在我們拿一個基因組 , 製作大約50個複製品 , 我們把所有的複製品都切成50個鹼基的讀取 , 然後我們將它們定序 , 大規模地平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把這些帶到軟體裡 , 重新組合起來 , 告訴你們這個故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	給大家看一下這個樣子 , 人類基因組計劃的樣子:3gabes , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一台機器在一週內運行:200gabes 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天將改變為600個 , 沒有任何一個步調減速的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 一個基地的價格 , 來定序一個基地 , 已經下跌了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這就等同於你在1998年用氣體填滿你的車 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開車到木星和後兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、定位、以及所有醫學文獻、摩爾定律、舊式定序的方式 , 這裡有全新的東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	傢伙 , 這是個部落格尺度 , 你通常不會看到像那樣往上走的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 今年全球人類基因組排序的能力大約有五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們根據被放置的機器 , 知道這一點 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	這是預期未來的兩倍、三倍 , 或四倍的一年 , 對可預見的未來而言 ,
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 特別有一間實驗室 , 代表了那能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因研究所
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人絕對能贏得這場新月球 , 順帶一提 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學來說意味著什麼 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以一個女人是37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她用 「 階段2 」 接受性乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和輻射治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她又帶著 「 階段三 」 卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療來治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後她在42歲時帶著更多的卵巢癌回來 , 更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著急性髓癌回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸道衰竭 , 死於八天後 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這個女人被治療的方式 , 只有十年的時間 , 會看起來像在血液中 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	而是因為像我同事rickwilson這樣的人 , 在華盛頓大學的基因研究所 , 她決定要看這位女士的後期 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他的基因定序 , 取出皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 和癌症骨髓 , 他將兩者的全部基因組定序 , 在幾週內 , 沒有什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	然後他把這兩個基因組在軟體中做比較 , 他發現 , 在其他東西中 , 是一個刪除 , 一個2000個核酸刪除 , 在300億個鹼基中 , 一個叫做tp53的特定基因 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因中有這種惡劣的突變 , 你一生中有百分之九十的機率會得到癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	所以 , 不幸的是 , 這並不能幫助這位女性 , 但它確實有嚴重的 , 深遠的影響到她的家庭 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 他們就會得到這個基因檢測 , 然後他們會了解 , 那麼他們就可以去取得普通的螢幕 , 並且能夠早期捕捉到癌症 , 有可能顯著地活得更久 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我介紹一下啤酒雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時被診斷出腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的媽媽是一位非常勇敢的女人 , 她不相信症狀不符合 , 透過一些英勇的努力和許多網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫療社群 , 事實上 , 他們還有別的 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的是預防性失調 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了dopa , 他們的症狀確實改善了 , 但他們並沒有完全不正常 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	結果這張照片裡的先生是一位叫joebeery的傢伙 , 他很幸運能成為一家叫生命科技的公司的學者 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是兩家公司之一 , 讓這些龐大的基因組定序工具
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他的做法是讓他的孩子進行測序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現 , 在一個叫做spr的基因中 , 一系列的突變 , 它負責製造血清素 , 在其他東西中產生血清素 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 在左右 , 他們給了這些孩子一種血清素先驅藥物 , 現在效果很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 在沒有完整基因序列的情況下 , 這絕對不會發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	幾年前 , 這要花十萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美金 。 明年是一千美金 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	一百元後的一年 , 給或一年
that's how fast this is moving .	這移動的速度就是這麼快 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有小小的尼克喜歡蝙蝠俠和戒槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果 , 尼克在兒童醫院出現 , 腹部像飢荒的受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	不是說他沒有吃東西 , 而是當他吃東西的時候 , 他的腸道基本上會打開 , 糞便會從他的腸子裡吐出來 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	所以 , 一百次手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽媽 , 請祈禱我 。 我在這麼多的痛苦中 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好在臨床遺傳學上有一個背景 , 他完全不知道發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓我們讓這個孩子的基因組定序 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現 , 在一個控制細胞死亡的基因中 , 單一的突變 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以 , 理論是 , 他對於食物本質上發生的事 , 有些免疫反應 , 那是自然的反應 , 這會造成一些程式化的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但規範下面的基因卻被打破了 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	當然 , 這也說明了骨髓移植的治療 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	九個月以後 , 他現在用a1醬料吃牛排了 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	將基因組當作一個普遍診斷的前景 , 今天正朝我們而來 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 在這裡
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	對我們所有人來說 , 這意味著在座的每個人 , 可以多活五年、十年、二十年 , 只因為這一件事 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你想到地球上人類的足跡 , 以及我們維持糧食生產的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	結果發現 , 同樣的科技也被用來種植玉米、小麥、大豆 , 以及其他高容忍乾旱、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑的作物 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	現在看 , 只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就得要繼續成長、吃基因改造的食物 , 那是我今天唯一要採用的位置 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	danielkraftdemos他的骨髓礦工一個新裝置 , 它很快就收集了救命骨髓 , 和捐贈者最小的痛苦 。 他強調在骨髓中找到的成人幹細胞 , 可以用來治療許多臨終條件 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。
