now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	去年jillboltetaylor得到啟發 , 我沒有帶一個人腦 , 但我確實帶了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓其實就是我們用來拯救數萬名病人的性命 , 大部分患有先進的惡性惡性病例如白血病和淋巴瘤和其他一些疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛進行我的移植計畫 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室 。 我們這裡有bob , 誰是志工捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國去拯救白血病的孩子 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以實際上我們要如何收割這塊骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 一般的麻醉 , 護士 , 還有另一位醫生 , 來自我 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	bob在桌上 , 我們把這一類的小針 , 你知道的 , 不是太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們的方法是將它放到軟組織中 , 將它打到硬骨中 , 進入tuchus這個技術術語 , 並且每次使用針筒 , 激發大約十個骨髓的磁鐵 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	將它交給護士 , 她將它戒掉成一丁點 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	將它交回我 。 我們一而再再而三地這麼做 。
about 200 times usually .	大約兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	到了最後 , 我的手臂很棒 , 我手上有一通電話 , 更不用說bob , 他的尾巴看起來更像這樣 , 像是瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這個程序在40年內並沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能有更好的方法來做這件事
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到一個微創入侵的方法 , 一個我們稱之為骨髓礦工的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓礦工 , 這裡的運作方式
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準鋸子病人
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭數十次 , 我們只進入一次 , 進入臀部或臀部的前面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個彈性、有力的導管 , 有一個特別的電線迴圈 , 留在骨髓的部分內 , 跟著臀部的輪廓 , 隨著它移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以 , 它能讓你快速地抱負 , 或吸取 , 很快地透過一個洞 , 豐富的骨髓 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過相同的入口
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , bob只能得到一個穿刺 , 當地的麻醉 , 把這個收割當成一個病人 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 。 我在史丹佛拿到一個小小的學金 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再玩一下這個 。
and our team members developed this technology .	而我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到了兩種大型動物 , 豬的研究
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 令我們驚訝的是 , 我們不只拿到骨髓 , 還拿到骨髓中的幹細胞活動十倍 , 從骨髓礦工得到的幹細胞活動 , 和正常裝置相比 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年剛剛被食品及藥物管理局批准
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡是活的病患 , 你可以看到它跟著彈性的曲線
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病患身上 , 會有兩次通過 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在本地麻醉下做的 , 作為一個病人 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	我們再次得到 , 比起同一個病人所做的標準方法 , 多出3到6倍的幹細胞 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	那你為什麼要在乎呢 ? 骨髓是一種非常豐富的成人幹細胞來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但尚未進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞在我們體內 , 包括我們骨髓中的血液幹細胞 , 這種幹細胞已經被我們用作一種幹細胞療法 , 已經超過四十年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去的十年裡 , 骨髓幹細胞的爆炸 , 來治療病人的其他疾病 , 比如心臟病、血管疾病、口服器、組織工程 , 甚至神經學 , 用來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出來 , 商業化 , 今年 , 世代2.0位骨髓礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望能得到更多幹細胞 , 哪些轉譯成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	可能會鼓勵更多人登記 , 成為可能救命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可能促使你銀行自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你更年輕、更健康時 , 在未來你應該需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後這張照片是我們的骨髓移植倖存者每年在史丹佛聚集在一起
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項科技能讓我們未來有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者garretlisi對宇宙有爭議性的新模型 , 只能回答所有大問題 。 如果沒有其他問題 , 就是最漂亮的8維度模型 , 是你所見過最美麗的基本粒子和力量 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、科技、
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garretlisi理論在他的一切理論上
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看那些殺手方程式 。 甜心 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	其實 , 接下來的18分鐘 , 我要盡我所能地描述粒子物理的美好 , 不用方程式 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們可以從珊瑚身上學到很多 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一個珊瑚頭都包含成千上萬的聚合物 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些聚合物會不斷繁殖 , 分成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是一個超智能的珊瑚 , 我們就可以單獨的一個個體 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個特定的地點和他的鄰居相比 , 如果只是機會 , 或命運 , 又怎樣 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們調整溫度太高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以相當地表示 , 你看 , 我有衝浪疤可以證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個聚合物會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居很明顯是他一模一樣的複製品 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在其他的地點 , 但經歷他們是獨立的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 一個超級智慧的珊瑚會獨特的準備去了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙運作方式 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們我們的現實是持續分支到不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說 , 這是一件奇怪的事 , 可以包容我們的心靈 , 因為我們只能體驗一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子怪異最初是由埃爾文•薛丁格和他的貓所描述的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓更喜歡這個版本
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設備中 , 薛丁格在一個有放射性樣本的箱子裡 , 由量子力學的定律所組成 , 分支成一個放射線的狀態 , 和一個沒有的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在這個樣本放射線中 , 它會引發一個觸發 , 釋放毒藥和薛丁格已死 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些現實是被每個個體分開的 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	到目前為止 , 另一個也不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說似乎很奇怪 , 因為我們每個人都只經歷一個個別的存在 , 而我們不見到其他分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就好像我們每個人 , 像薛丁格 , 是種珊瑚分支 , 進入不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這是世界在小規模的運作方式
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	可以用單一句話來總結:所有可能發生的一切 , 確實 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不意味著一切都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理則是要描述哪些可能發生 , 以及哪些事不能 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理告訴我們的是 , 一切都歸功於幾何學 , 以及基本粒子的互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	唯有這些互動是完全平衡的 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我先來說明我們對這些粒子的認識 , 它們是什麼 , 以及這個平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一束質子和反質子會加速到接近光速 , 並在撞擊中聚集 , 產生出純能量的爆炸 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴霧 , 有偵測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器--在日內瓦的大型強子對撞機有十七英里--當它在運作時 , 畫出五倍的電力 , 和蒙特瑞市一樣 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法明確預測哪些粒子會在任何個別碰撞中產生
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都意識到
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理的確告訴我們 , 哪些粒子可以產生
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子一定跟質子和反質子所攜帶的質量和能量一樣多
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這個能量限制還大的粒子 , 都沒有產生出來 , 且對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新粒子加速器如此令人興奮的原因 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將推動這個能量限制了七倍以外所做過的事 , 所以我們很快就會看到一些新粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能會看到什麼之前 , 讓我來描述我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一整個亞原子粒子的動物園
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大多數人都熟悉電子
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這房間裡的許多人 , 都讓一個好的生活推動他們 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有一個中立的夥伴叫做微中子 , 沒有電荷和一個非常小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上城的夸克有非常大的質量 , 並在三分之內結合 , 讓原子內部的質子和中子變得更大 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都出現在左邊和右邊的品種中 , 有攜帶相反電荷的反粒子夥伴 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也有較少的第二代和第三代相同的載荷量卻有較高的質量
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子都和各種力量的粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力透過稱為光子的粒子與電荷相互作用
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	也有一種非常微弱的力量 , 很不想像的 , 弱的力量 , 只能和左撇子互動 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	強力在夸克間作用 , 帶著不同種類的載荷 , 稱為顏色荷 , 帶著三種不同的品種:紅、綠、藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann為這些名字-他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 有重力的力量 , 藉由質量和旋轉來互動物質 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	這裡最要了解的是 , 每種力量都有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量與物質相互作用 , 根據每個粒子所擁有的相對應載荷 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被看見的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 會給所有其他粒子帶來質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是看到這種希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎肯定會 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的謎團是我們可能看到的
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我將向你們展示一個美麗的可能性 , 來到這場演講的結尾 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用它們的旋轉和載荷來計算這些不同的粒子 , 總共有226個 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	這樣大量的粒子才能持續追蹤
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然有好多基本粒子似乎很奇怪 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的載荷來繪製它們 , 一些美麗的圖案就會出現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 一個負電 , 夸克有三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以 , 當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克結合成一個質子 , 它的電荷總加上一個 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷其實是另外兩個載荷的組合:超荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們將超荷和弱荷分散到這個二維載荷空間中的粒子載荷 , 電荷就是這些粒子沿著垂直方向坐在那裡 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力會根據超荷和弱荷相互作用 , 產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這被稱為 「 統一式電路模型 」 , 它在1967年被放在一起 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們大部分人只熟悉電荷 , 而不是這兩者都是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊這裡的希格斯有很大的質量 , 打破了這個電擊模式的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它使弱力變得非常弱 , 通過給弱粒子一個大質量 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	既然這個巨大的希格斯坐在地平線的方向 , 電磁主義的光子仍然沒有質量 , 並在載荷空間中與電荷相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以 , 電磁力和弱力是被這種在二維空間中的粒子載荷的模式所描述 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力推廣出它的兩個載荷方向 , 並沿著這些方向繪製出力粒子的載荷 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四維載荷空間中被繪製出來 , 投射到像這樣的二維空間 , 讓我們可以看到它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子互動時 , 大自然就會讓東西保持完美的平衡 , 沿著這四個載荷方向 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果一顆粒子和反粒子碰撞 , 它會產生一股能量爆炸 , 以及四個載荷方向的總載荷量為零 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時 , 任何東西都可以被創造出來只要它有相同的能量並維持為零的總載荷
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 載荷一定永遠保持平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個微弱的粒子可以腐化成一個電子和一個反中子 , 這三種仍然會加到零總載荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	自然總是保持著完美的平衡
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些載荷的模式並不只是漂亮的
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們什麼互動是允許發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間旋轉這個載荷空間以更好的角度看強度的交互作用這個有著不錯的六角形對稱性
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強烈的互動中 , 一個強力粒子 , 例如這個 , 和一個有色夸克互動 , 例如這個綠色的夸克 , 給一個有不同顏色載荷的夸克 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	而強烈的互動每秒鐘發生在我們體內的每一個原子核中 , 把原子核黏在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷對應三種力量並不是故事的結局 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們也可以將兩種載荷與重力相對應 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們納入這些時 , 每個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉載荷 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以他們都分開 , 在六度載荷空間中給一個不錯的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看看它相當漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這個模式符合我們目前最好的知識 , 關於大自然如何建構在這些小小的粒子之中 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們肯定知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子在實驗中達到的極限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式中 , 我們已經知道這些小尺度的粒子物理 。 宇宙和這些小尺度運作的方式是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些我們還不知道的事情的新舊想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們只想用數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能不能把我們的手拿到整體芝加拉達 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想找到所有製造我們宇宙的完整圖像的粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張照片來預測我們在實驗達到更高能量時會看到的新粒子 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以在粒子物理學中有一個舊的想法這個已知的載荷模式不太對稱 , 可以從一個更完美的模式中浮現出來 , 和希格斯粒子如何破解電磁圖案的方式類似 , 來賦予電磁主義 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這點 , 我們需要用新的載荷方向介紹新力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹一個新的方向時 , 我們會猜測粒子沿著這個方向載荷什麼 , 然後我們可以與他人一起旋轉它 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜測 , 我們可以在六度載荷中建構出標準載荷作為一個破碎的對稱性 , 在七個載荷維度中 , 將這個更完美的模式建構在七個載荷維度中 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這個特別的選擇對應於1973年巴蒂和薩拉姆的一個大統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們觀察這個新的統一模式 , 我們可以看到一些粒子似乎缺少的落差 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	一個物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的圖案 , 將被建立的圖案視為一個 「 次 」 的圖案 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的圖案讓我們能夠預測從未被看見的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這種統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 這應該很像弱力 , 只有弱力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這組載荷 , 考慮到關於物質粒子的奇怪事實:物質的第二代和第三代物質擁有完全相同的載荷量 , 和第一代的載荷空間 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不是獨一無二的被它們的六個載荷分辨出來的 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準載荷空間的上方 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那麼我們可以分配每個粒子獨特的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個圖案是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到第二代和第三代物質有關聯 , 一個叫做 「 試驗性 」 的對稱性 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	這種八度空間的載荷模式 , 其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構的一部分 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的例外謊言團體的模式 , e8
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是平滑的 , 曲線形狀有248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	這個圖案中的每一點都對應到這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀的一個對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論的曲線時空 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	和量子力學一起 , 這個形狀的幾何學可以描述宇宙在最小尺度下如何運作的一切 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀生活在八度載荷空間的模式是精緻美麗的 , 它總結出上千種可能的交互作用在這些基本粒子之間 , 每一個都只是這個複雜形狀的一個面向 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉它時 , 我們可以看到許多其它錯綜複雜的圖案包含在這個圖案中 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	藉由一個特定的旋轉 , 我們可以從這個圖案中看出 , 沿著一個對稱軸的八維度 , 同時看到所有的粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是個非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何統一 , 我們可以看到一些洞 , 在那裡 , 新粒子是由這個圖案所需要的 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	這裡有20個空隙 , 新粒子應該是 , 其中兩個已經被帕塔拉姆粒子給填補了 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從他們在這個模式的位置 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是像希格斯粒子一樣的擴展場 , 但有顏色的載荷 , 並和強力互動 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子完成了這個模式 , 給我們完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有非常深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是個絕妙的前景 , 這種偉大的數學美的物體可以用最小尺度來描述粒子互動的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	而大自然被數學描述的這個想法並不是全新的想法 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年 , 伽利略寫下這句話: 「 大自然的宏偉書 , 這本書一直開放給我們的凝視 , 是以數學的語言寫的 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形 , 和其他幾何圖形 , 沒有人類是不可能理解它的單一字詞的 ; 沒有這些 , 有一個在黑暗迷宮中徘徊 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我曾試著遵循伽利略的指導 , 描述粒子物理學的數學只用三角形、圓形和其他的幾何圖形 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我真的在研究這些東西時 , 數學可以組成一個黑暗的迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但 , 放心的是 , 在這個數學的核心是純潔的 , 漂亮的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入量子力學 , 這個數學描述我們的宇宙是一塊正在成長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在所有可能的位置都在交互作用 , 根據一個美麗的圖案 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的模式可以用像大型強子對撞機一樣大的新機器來看 , 我們或許可以看出大自然是否使用這種e8圖案 , 或不一樣的圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程 , 是參與其中的美好冒險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合e8模式的粒子那會非常、非常酷
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到了新粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那會非常有趣 , 但對這個e8理論不好 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會有多糟呢 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 相當糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然如何運作是非常冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的理論
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多辛苦的工作 , 知道大部分這些想法 , 最後可能不會成為大自然的真相 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣:有許多野生動物 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論很像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	以任何大型投資來說 , 若不在工作時 , 要放棄一線研究 , 可能會很有情感 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學界 , 如果有些東西不有效 , 你就得把它丟出去 , 試試其他的東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 唯一維持清潔和達成快樂的方法 , 在這個不確定性中 , 就是保持平衡和觀點在生活中 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我盡我所能過著平衡的生活
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我的人生 , 平衡在物理、愛和衝浪我自己的三個載荷方向之間 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	如此一來 , 就算我所從事的物理 , 我仍然知道我過著美好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	而我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去10年來 , 我大部分都住在毛伊島 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在是宇宙中最偉大的謎團之一 , 對我父母來說 , 我如何在全職工作中存活下來 , 卻無時無刻無刻無所不在 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要讓你們知道那個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊的家裡辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到這些美麗的景象是相似的 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊的家和辦公室
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我曾經選擇過非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心房租讓我花時間做我喜愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	過著遊牧的存在 , 很多時候都很艱難 , 但這讓我能住在美麗的地方 , 保持平衡 , 在我的生活中 , 我一直很快樂 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我可以花很多時間跟超智能珊瑚掛在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級智慧人士的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以我很高興能在這裡受邀來ted
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概了解其中的2% , 但我仍然很喜歡 。 所以我要聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬物理論-garretlisi:我習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克里斯:沒錯 。 它之所以會讓少數人感到興奮 , 是因為 , 如果你是對的 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是說我們應該把宇宙想成是最小的可能性嗎 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小尺度上有沒有比例 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	蓋爾:嗯 , 現在我給你看的模式 , 與我們所知的基本粒子物理相對應 , 已經對應到一個非常美麗的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這也是我說我們肯定知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這個形狀有著驚人的相似性 , 它符合e8模式的方式 , 可能是圖片的其他部分 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些圖案 , 其實代表了這個高維物體的對稱性 , 它會在我們經歷的時空中移動和跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	那就是解釋我們所看到的這些基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克里斯:但弦理論家 , 如我所知 , 用更小的弦來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們應該如何看一個與e8有關的電子呢 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	格林:不 , 這會是這個e8形狀的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 隨著時空移動的形狀 , 它會扭轉 。 當它移動時 , 它會扭轉的方向就是我們所看到的粒子 。 所以它會是──克:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子的大小如何連結 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	變大了嗎 ? 小了嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	蓋爾:嗯 , 就我們所知電子就是點粒子 , 所以這會降到最小可能的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 這些東西在量子場理論中被解釋的方式是 , 所有的可能性都同時擴大和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我用類比來珊瑚
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8會以這種形狀連接在時空中每一刻
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說 , 形狀會扭轉方向 , 形狀會在曲線的表面上轉動 , 正是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以 , 透過量子場理論 , 它們將自己呈現為點 , 並以那樣的方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我是否能讓這一切更清楚
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克里斯:這並不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	這引發了一種奇妙的感覺 , 我當然想更了解這一點 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但謝謝你來了 。 這真的很棒 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇的黑猩猩研究員珍•古拉爾談到塔卡爾和她的其他社區計畫 , 協助波普非洲城鎮的人們 , 和受威脅的動物生活在旁邊 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍.古拉爾幫助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 雅博 , 古博 , 古博 , 邦索爾 , 但我們也可以 , ooh , oh , oh , oh , ooh , oh , oh , oh , oh , oh , oh 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這就是黑猩猩在晚上睡前所發出的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一邊傳到另一邊 , 從一群蜂巢傳到下一組 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	我今天晚上想跟我談的演講 , 來自昨天的zeray所離開的地點 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個了不起、三歲的澳洲孩童賽拉姆 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過關於歷史、家族樹 , 透過基因側寫來表達人類 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	那是古生物學家 , 路易斯•李克 , 他讓我踏上研究黑猩猩的路徑 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	那時還蠻特別的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	這有點常見 , 但他的論點是因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石遺跡 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以從化石中分辨出那些人的樣子 , 從肌肉附著的形狀 , 關於他們從各式各樣的工藝品中找到的東西 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但牠們的行為呢 ? 這是他想知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他爭論並現在是相當普遍的理論如果我們在我們最接近的生物親戚身上發現行為模式或相同的行為模式 , 即人類的偉大猿 , 那麼或許這些行為在七百萬年前出現在猿類、人類的祖先身上
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 或許我們從古老、古老的過去帶給了我們這些特質 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看看現今處理人類演化的教科書 , 你通常會發現人們在推測人類早期的行為 , 根據黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	它們和我們相比 , 比起任何其他活生生的生物 , 我們在這次的ted大會中聽說過 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以這對我來說 , 對於黑猩猩和我們很像 , 對於牠們行為的某些方面 , 它仍然會留下評論 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每隻黑猩猩都有他或她自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給了他們名字 。 他們可以活到六十歲以上 , 雖然我們認為大部分的人可能不會在野外賺到六十歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃茲先生 。 雌性在11或12歲時 , 生下了第一個嬰兒 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她每五六年只有一個嬰兒 , 一個很長的童年依賴期間 , 當孩子在護理時 , 晚上和母親一起睡覺 , 然後騎在她背上 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 這麼長的童年對黑猩猩很重要 , 就如同我們 , 和學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同動物的演化過程中變得更加複雜 , 所以我們發現 , 學習在一個個體的生命歷史中扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	而年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間觀看他們的長者所做的事 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道他們有能力模仿他們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 用這種方式 , 現今在所有不同黑猩猩族群中看到的不同工具行為 , 研究非洲這些行為如何從一代傳到下一代 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 如此一來 , 我們就能把這些工具行為描述成原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語 。 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	他們的確有很豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 很多都很相似 , 甚至和我們一模一樣 , 形成在相同的情境中 。 迎接黑猩猩們擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也親吻 , 握手 , 相互拍打 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	然後他們會游泳 , 然後扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們會發現許多慈悲的例子 , 例如愛和真正的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 對他們的天性有黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	它們具有極度殘酷的能力 , 甚至是一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些極具侵略性的行為 , 最多的部分 , 是對鄰近社會群體的個體進行指導 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們非常有侵略性 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩們 , 我相信 , 比起其他任何生物 , 已經幫助我們了解 , 畢竟人類和動物王國之間沒有明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 隨時愈來愈模糊 , 當我們觀察到更多 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我1960年開始的研究還在持續進行中 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些黑猩猩 , 生活在野外 , 過著複雜的社會生活 , 幫助超過其他任何東西 , 讓我們了解到我們是其中的一部分 , 而不是和我們共享地球的驚人動物分開 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以很難過發現黑猩猩就像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 正在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張從空中拍攝的照片 , 它展示給你們看gombe的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	大約十六年前 , 我飛越整個區域 , 發現在公園外 , 這片森林 , 在1960年 , 在坦尚尼卡湖的東岸 , 幾乎沒有破壞 , 沿著坦尚尼卡湖的東岸 , 那裡是小小的、三十平方公園的全國公園 , 一個問題來到我心中 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何試圖拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 , 當居住在國家公園附近的人努力求生存 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	居住的人口比土地還可能支持 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民的數量不斷增加 , 從布洛伊和剛果湖中湧入 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人他們負擔不起從別處購買食物
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為tacare 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	用一種非常全面的方式來改善住在公園附近村莊裡的人的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	從12個村莊開始 , 現在已經24年了 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入探究 , 但它包括樹木護理、養殖最適合的方法 , 到現在已經非常低落 , 幾乎像沙漠一樣的土地在這些山中 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、預防土壤侵蝕的方法
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重新利用過度使用的農田的方式 , 這樣在兩年內 , 它們就能再次有生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	努力幫助村民從井中取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建立了一些教室
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 與小群婦女合作 , 提供他們小額貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	如同世界各地的案例 , 大約95%的貸款回報 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性權力 , 與教育一起工作 , 提供獎學金給女孩們 , 讓他們能完成二年級的學校 , 在明確了解 , 在全世界各地 , 隨著女性的教育改善 , 家庭規模大小的下降 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這個計畫的結果 , 有些事情正在進行保育 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的狀況是 , 住在這24個村莊的農夫 , 而不是把我們當成一群白人來研究一群猴子 , 順帶一提 , 許多工作人員現在是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始塔卡爾計畫時 , 是個坦尚尼亞的團隊進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦尚尼亞團隊和村民談話 , 問他們對什麼有興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育有興趣嗎 ? 絕對沒有 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 當他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更加了解保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 隨著山丘的上層被砍伐了樹木 , 所以你有了這可怕的土壤侵蝕和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在開發我們所謂的更大的gombe生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是在國家公園外的一塊區域 , 伸展到這些非常退化的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村莊有更好的生活標準 , 他們其實同意把10%到20%的土地放在高地的一邊 , 這樣一來 , 當樹木長回來後 , 黑猩猩就會有葉廊 , 穿過它們可以在國家公園以外的其他遺傳族群和其他遺傳族群之間的交流 。
so tacare is a success .	所以 , 塔卡爾是個成功 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其他地方複製它 , 圍繞著其他的荒野地區 , 面臨極端的人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 如同我們這前幾天所討論的 , 都是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有很大的貧窮 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你得到大量居住的土地 , 並不是那麼肥沃 , 特別是當你砍伐樹木時 , 土壤會開放給侵蝕風 , 如同絕望的族群 , 砍伐更多的樹木 , 這樣他們就能嘗試為自己和家人種植食物 , 會發生什麼事 ? 有些事必須給予 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	而另一個問題不只在非洲 , 還有其他發展中國家的國家 , 確實 , 到處都是我們對地球做了什麼事 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 著名的科學家 , e.o.威爾森說如果這個星球上的每一個人都能維持一般歐洲人或美國人的生活水準 , 我們需要三個新星球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們在說四個 。 但我們沒有 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 這裡的問題是 , 我們是 , 可以說是地球上最有智慧的 , 擁有這個非凡的大腦 , 能夠被這些ted大會所描繪出來的科技 , 然而我們卻破壞了我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做了重大決定之前 , 曾經圍坐著問自己: 「 這個決定如何影響我們的人民七代領先 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 重大的決定 , 我在這裡不特別談非洲 , 而是已開發國家的重大決定 , 包含了數百萬美元 , 數百萬人 , 通常是基於 「 這會如何影響下一次股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	而這些決定會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始到非洲各地旅行 , 談論黑猩猩所面臨的問題 , 以及牠們消失的森林時 , 我了解到更多的非洲問題 , 可能在前殖民時代剝削的大門上 , 可能造成更多問題 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始到非洲外面旅行 , 在歐洲談話 , 在美國談話 , 到亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	而且你知道我所說的那種 , 我指的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水也許是這個世紀我們將面臨的最關鍵的議題之一 , 到處都有水被農業、工業和家庭的化學物質污染 , 這些化學物質仍然在世界各地被噴灑 , 似乎有能力從過去經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林正在被砍伐 ; 像海嘯這樣的效應變得更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤侵蝕
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們和其他溫室氣體的化石燃燒毫無關聯 , 所以 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界的人都開始相信我們的氣候有問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候都混合在一起 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而且是受影響較差的窮人
it's africa that already is affected .	已經受到影響的非洲
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱的狀況更糟 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨來臨時 , 通常會導致洪水和增加苦惱 , 以及貧窮和飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	而居住的人們數量卻無法支撐土地太貧窮 , 無法購買食物 , 不能搬走 , 因為整個土地已經退化了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化 , 令人毛骨悚然 , 隨著樹木的最後一端被砍伐 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不只在非洲 , 全世界都有 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不驚訝 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇見了好多年輕人 , 他們似乎失去了希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎已經失去了智慧 , 是原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為在這個非凡聰明的大腦中可以有些不相干嗎 ? ted科技的範圍內 , 和人類的心 ? 用非科學的角度來談談它 , 在愛和同情之間 。 是否有一些不相干的連結 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們不是憂鬱或冷淡 , 或苦惱和生氣 。 他們說的一樣東西 , 或多或少都這樣說: 「 我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 沒有任何我們能做的 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們 , 我想我們從他們那個年紀開始對這個美麗的星球造成傷害 , 我感覺到這個絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	導致這個計畫 , 我們稱之為根與芽 , 它從坦尚尼亞開始 , 到目前為止 , 遍及全世界97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	這是象徵性的 。 根基製造了堅定的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射擊似乎很小 ; 為了抵達太陽它們能穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆當作我們在地球上遇到的這些問題 , 環境和社會問題 。 這是希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地成千上萬的年輕人都能突破 , 並且能為所有生物創造一個更美好的世界 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要的訊息:我們每一個人每一天都會做出改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有一個選擇 。 在座的每一個人 , 我們都有一個選擇 , 選擇我們想要做出什麼樣的不同 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	窮人沒有選擇 , 我們要改變事情 , 這樣窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽團體全都選擇了三個項目
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們有多老 , 哪個國家 , 不論他們在城市或鄉下 , 都要看什麼樣的計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有從幼兒園到大學的計畫 , 有越來越多的成人開始自己的根與芽團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	而每一組都選擇 , 在它們之間 , 三種不同的項目 , 來讓這個更美好的世界 , 認識到所有這些不同的問題都是互相關聯的 , 並互相對立 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以他們的其中一個計畫會是幫助他們自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們能夠的話 , 他們可能會募集資金來幫助世界其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一項計畫是幫助動物 , 不只是野生動物 , 馴養動物也是 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們的其中一個計畫將會幫助我們共同的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	所有這些都是學習和平與和諧的訊息 , 在我們的家庭、我們的社區、國家、文化、宗教、宗教之間 , 和自然世界之間的訊息 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然的世界 。 我們不能以我們現在的速度去破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們的確比這個星球還多 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只要在非洲這裡挑選一兩個計畫 , 根與芽團體都在做 , 一兩個專案只在坦尚尼亞、肯亞、南非、剛果巴拉扎維爾、獅子山共和國、喀麥隆 , 和其他團體 。 如我所說 , 它在世界上的97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們種植樹木 , 種植有機蔬菜
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 和雞一起賣蛋 , 為了賺一點錢 , 或只是用它們來餵飽家人 , 並感受到一種自豪和賦權的感覺 , 因為他們不再對他人無助 , 只靠蔬菜和雞 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理上的幫助 , 給予士兵們 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做這樣的項目是把他們從自己身上帶出來 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會中有用的成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有更多根與芽的時間了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽的重要要素 , 年紀較大的孩子和年輕的孩子交談 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	而沒有預防懷孕之類的年輕人會從其他年輕人那裡傾聽更好而不是成人
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這是我在世界各地問的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你看過你的黑猩猩數目大約從一百萬分之一開始 , 在本世紀的轉捩點 , 到現在沒有超過十五萬隻 , 和其他許多動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林正在消失 , 沙漠曾經是森林的地方 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? " 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣的會議 , 也沒有希望 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是這個驚人的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	而我是說 , 想想科技
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	最後我很興奮 , 最後 , 來找大家談堆肥的廁所 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只是把這些水沖下海底 , 太糟糕了 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	然後討論再生能源迫切重要的事 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們關心地球為我們的孩子嗎 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	我們當中有多少人有小孩或孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們關心他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們 , 身為世界各地的菁英 , 我們能為此做點什麼 。 我們可以為我們每天生活的方式做出選擇 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼 , 穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用問題來做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	在他或她長大後 , 會如何影響我的孩子 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或我的孫子 , 或不論是什麼
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦和人類的心結合在一起 , 我們加入了全世界的手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	ted就是這樣幫助我們的 , google也幫助我們 , esri也幫助我們繪製gombe國家公園 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們可以使用的科技
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	今天下午你們已經聽過了 , 開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 看到我們一定要有的改變 , 如果我們關心未來 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	希望自然的下一個原因是驚人的韌性 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以拿一個完全被破壞的區域 , 隨著時間 , 或許有些幫助它可以再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	而一個例子就是tacare計畫 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴你 , 看似死去的樹木木木木材 , 如果你停止給它們駭客 , 那你不需要因為木材很多 , 那麼在五年內 , 你可以有一棵30英尺長的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎在滅絕的邊緣上 , 可以得到第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它很有啟發性 。 它帶給我的最後一個範疇希望 , 我們在過去的兩天中聽說過這點:這個不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這決心的人類精神 , 人類精神的韌性 , 使你認為會被貧窮、疾病給打擊的人 , 或其他的人 , 可以自拔 , 有時可以用手 , 把他們拉出來 , 把他們自己的部分帶到社會中 , 改變世界 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想看 , 非洲外有一兩個人真的很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出很長的清單 , 但顯然納爾遜•曼德拉從十七年的硬體勞工出現 , 23年的監禁能力 , 帶著這驚人的寬恕能力 , 讓他能夠帶領他的國家走出種族隔離的邪惡政權 , 沒有血保 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	住在奈及利亞的肯薩尼瓦 , 他接下了巨型石油公司 , 雖然全世界的人都試過他們最好的 , 卻被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人如此激勵人心
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人是年輕非洲人需要的榜樣 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環保的榜樣 , 今天我也聽過其中一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我很感激這個機會再次與ted的每個人分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中的一些人能聚在一起討論這些事 , 特別是根與芽的方案 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	這位年輕女子正經營這整個會議中心的最後一個字 , 我今天見到她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她對她的認證感到非常興奮 。 她是根與芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在daressalaam的領導階層
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這幫助她做她正在做的事
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 很振奮我去見她 , 看到一個例子 , 說明年輕人如何 , 當他們被賦予權力 , 給予採取行動的機會 , 讓這個世界變得更好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家戴安娜.柯恩分享了一些艱難的事實 , 關於海洋中的塑膠污染 , 以及我們生活中的一些想法 , 關於如何從塑膠垃圾漩渦中解放自己 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、任務藍色、海洋、塑膠等 ,
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜.柯恩:關於塑膠污染的艱難事實 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在和塑膠袋一起工作 , 我剪裁並縫合在一起 , 作為我藝術作品的主要材料 , 過去20年來 ,
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成2和3d的碎片和雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	與塑膠一起工作 , 大約在前八年 , 我的一些作品開始裂縫 , 分解成更小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太好了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	跟我們一樣是平默的 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	教育我自己更進一步 , 關於塑膠 , 我其實意識到這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠會分解成小塊 , 因為它一直是塑膠的 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 很多是在海洋環境中
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	過去幾年 , 我學會了太平洋垃圾堆和健身房 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	而我最初的反應和我認為這是很多人對學習的第一個反應是: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們必須走出去 , 清理這個東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以我實際上開發了一個提案 , 用一艘貨船和兩艘被拆解的漁船拖網 , 一艘吊車 , 一台拖車 , 和一台冷模機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	而我的意圖是要走出健身房 , 提高對這個議題的意識 , 並開始把塑膠拿起來 , 把它放進一些位元和冷的模塊中 , 變成可能用來做為基礎社區的建材 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和那些曾經去過健身房的人談話 , 研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 並且去做 , 我發現 , 事實上 , 清理它會是一個非常小的滴水滴 , 相對於全世界每天產生的量 , 我需要回頭看 , 看看更大的照片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的照片是:我們需要找到一個可以關掉水龍頭的方法 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切割單眼和可丟棄的塑膠 , 每天都要進入海洋環境 , 以全球規模進入 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著這點 , 我也了解到我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心在太平洋中部的塑膠塑膠 , 我知道現在有11個健身房 , 可能是世界上五個主要海洋中的塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不僅僅是我所關心的塑膠垃圾堆中塑膠的健身房
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 我所有的食物都包在塑膠上 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都包在塑膠裡 , 甚至在健康食物市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也關心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 我關心塑膠和塑膠從塑膠滲入我們體內的毒素 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群其他人一起研究這個議題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多我們正在努力的倡議 , 但其中有些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	一是:如果我們在海洋中發現的有80%到90%是海洋碎片 , 我們在海洋中發現的就是塑膠 , 那為什麼我們不稱它為
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收每個人的書 , 以永續發展和綠化為主題 , 以回收的概念為主題 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把某樣東西放進去 , 再也不用想了 。
what is the reality of that ?	到底是怎麼一回事 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 我們的塑膠回收量不到7% 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真正深入探討 , 特別是當涉及到塑膠瓶時 , 大部分只會被降低 , 或被刺殺 , 或被運送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被降低 , 轉換成更少的東西 , 玻璃瓶可以再次成為玻璃瓶 , 或可以再次使用塑膠瓶 , 不能再當塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大議題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一個我們正在看的 , 請大家思考的是 , 我們已經在 「 減少、再利用、回收 」 的前面加上第四個環 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	每當可能 , 拒絕單調和可丟棄的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案是存在的 ; 有些是非常老舊的 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我自己現在在收集這些酷炫的畢氏容器 , 使用這些裝置 , 而不是用來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和家人做服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易拿起一瓶不鏽鋼瓶或一瓶玻璃瓶 , 如果你在旅行 , 且你忘記帶著你的不鏽鋼瓶 , 再裝滿水 , 或過濾水 , 和購買塑膠瓶的水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想對在座的每個人說什麼我知道你們知道很多關於這個議題的你們都知道這在海洋中是個很大的問題但這是我們作為消費者所創造出來的問題我們可以解決
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以透過提高注意力來解決這個問題 , 並教導人們選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 不論何時 , 要選擇單一使用塑膠的替代品 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這些幹細胞的莖切入海洋中 , 這樣做 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的地球 , 拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這個來自pattiemaes在麻省理工學院的實驗室 , pranavftry駕駛的實驗是ted的buzz , 這是個可穿戴的裝置 , 用一個投影機來鋪設深度與我們的環境互動的方式 。 想像一下 , 「 少數族群報告 」 , 然後再來一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	demo , 設計 , 介面設計 , 科技 , 科技 ,
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	pattiemaes和pranav誤導演出第六感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我對這個問題很有興趣 , 我們是否能進化或發展出第六感 , 一種能讓我們無縫接觸、容易取得新陳代謝或資訊的感覺 , 可能存在於某處 , 可以協助我們做出正確的決定 , 來決定我們要面對的是什麼 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	在座有些人可能會爭辯 , 嗯 , 今天的手機已經不是這樣了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted見到某個人 , 這是最頂尖的網路位置 , 當然 , 在那一年 , 你不握某人的手 , 然後說: 「 你能容納一會兒 , 一會兒我拿出手機 , google搜尋你嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或是當你去超市的時候 , 你站在那一大堆不同類型的衛生紙上 , 你不會拿出你的手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 然後去一個網站 , 試著決定這些不同的衛生紙是最環保的購買方式 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們沒有很容易取得所有相關資訊 , 只要能協助我們做出最佳決策 , 關於接下來要做什麼 , 以及要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組一直在研發一系列的發明 , 讓我們能以一種簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡是要揭開我們最新的努力 , 目前為止最成功的努力 , 這在過程中還是很有用的 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	我現在戴著裝置 , 我們將它拼湊在一起 , 配合架子上的零件 , 順便說一下 , 在這一刻 , 只需花350美元 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著一台攝影機 , 只是一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜式的 , 電池驅動的投影系統 , 帶著一面小鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件在我口袋裡傳遞到我的手機 , 作為溝通和運算設備 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕納•弗特里 , 他真的是執行和設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走到任何表面 , 開始用手和前面投射的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統追蹤了四隻顯著的手指
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著你可能認得的簡單標記蓋 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要一個更時髦的版本你也可以用不同顏色來畫你的指甲 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上會追蹤這四根手指 , 辨識出他製作的任何手勢 , 以便他只能走進去 , 例如 , 一個長灘的地圖 , 放大 , 等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	這個系統也能辨識出有代表性的手勢 , 例如 「 拍照 」 的手勢 , 然後拍下你面前的任何東西 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以直接走到任何牆上 , 投射所有他所拍攝的照片 , 透過它們分類 , 並整理它們 , 等等 , 再一次 , 使用所有自然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	所以 , 有些人在兩年前來到這裡 , 看到jeffhan或一些人可能會想: 「 嗯 , 這看起來不像微軟的表面桌嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用自然的手勢互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的差別是你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走向任何表面 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西是可取得的 , 和這個投影資料互動的 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是完全可攜式的 , 可以是......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	所以 , 其中一個重要的差異是 , 它完全是移動式 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的差異是 , 在大量生產中 , 明天的成本不比現今的手機還高 , 實際上 , 更大的包裝看起來比我脖子上戴的版本還多 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但除了讓你們之外 , 有些人會幻想著 , 像tomcruise在《少數民族報告》中 , 我們對這個裝置感到很興奮的原因是 , 它真的可以作為這六感設備的其中一種 , 給你關於你眼前的任何資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	所以 , 我們看到帕納進入超市 , 他在購物一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一個產品--這個系統可以辨識出他所撿到的產品 , 使用圖像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以請求額外的資訊
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以這個特別的選擇是特別好的選擇 , 因為他個人的準則 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	在座有些人可能希望廁所的紙有最多白化的 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他可以拿到亞馬遜評分 , 它就會被投射到書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們先前的講者 , 順帶一提 , 在亞馬遜得到了很棒的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , pranav把書的頁面翻過來 , 然後再看到關於書讀者評論的額外資訊 , 也許是他最喜歡的評論家等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他轉到某個特定的頁面 , 他會發現一個意涵 , 一個我們朋友的意涵 , 給他一些額外的資訊 , 關於那個頁面上的任何東西 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀它從來沒有過時的報紙 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以得到你正在閱讀的影片註明你可以得到最新的運動分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是比較有爭議的一個
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你和ted的某個人互動時 , 也許你可以看到一個字雲 , 標籤的字眼 , 和那個人的部落格和個人網頁相關的字眼 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生對攝影機感興趣等等
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你去機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機路 , 它可以告訴你 , 你的飛行被延遲了 , 大門已經改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道現在的時光是什麼 , 就跟在你手臂上畫手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前正在發展的第六感 , 可以讓我們無縫接觸到所有相關的資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 真的 , 就像我說的 , 這背後的天才 。

and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	而他的女朋友可能也對他不太滿意 。
