and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 或許在另一十年內我們會在這裡與終極的第六感腦植入 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	phyllisrodriguez和aichael-wafi有一個強大的友誼 , 生於無法想像的失落 。 rodriguez的兒子在世貿中心被殺害 , 在2001年9月11日的世貿攻擊中被殺害 ; 艾瓦菲的兒子zacariasmoussaui被定罪 , 在那些攻擊中扮演著一個角色 , 希望能找到和平 , 這兩個媽們能了解並尊重彼此 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11的治癒:找到寬恕的媽媽 , 友情的友誼 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	phyllisrodriguez:我們今天來到這裡 , 是因為我們大部分人認為一個不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 現在我們感覺很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次發現我的兒子在2001年9月11日的世貿中心
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否曾在36小時後再度處罰 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治上的
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家要用我們兒子的名字 , 我的丈夫 , 奧蘭多 , 我和我們的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到 , 然而 , 透過衝擊 , 震驚 , 以及我們生命中可怕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們並沒有復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾週後 , 當zacariasmoussaoui在六個陰謀上被指出要承擔恐怖主義 , 美國政府向他要求死刑 , 如果定罪的話 , 我和我的丈夫反對了 , 公開場合 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些 , 透過人權團體 , 我們和其他幾個受害者的家人團結在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我看到媒體中的阿卡哈 , 來到她兒子被告知時 , 我心想: 「 多麼勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我想在我更堅強的時候遇到那個女人 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深處悲傷 , 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或者我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我的兒子是受害者時 , 我會馬上得到同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她的兒子被指控什麼時 , 她沒有得到那份同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的苦難和我一樣 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	所以 , 我們在2002年11月見面 , aicha現在會告訴你這是怎麼來的 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 女士們先生們
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmoussaoui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我請求 「 人權組織 」 讓我和受害者的父母聯絡 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我給五個家庭
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	然後我看到了phyllis , 我看著她
she was the only mother in the group .	她是群體中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他人則是兄弟姊妹
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我看到她就像我一樣的母親 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	身為母親 , 我受的許多苦 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結婚 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 一個十六歲的時候 , 第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以和zacarias的故事實在太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	而我仍然受苦 , 因為我的兒子就像是他活著一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為她的兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 。 我不知道他是否被折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	所以 , 這就是為什麼我決定說我的故事 , 所以我的苦難對其他女性來說是正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有婦女來說 , 所有賦予生命的媽媽 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	由於我們是女性 , 因為我們是女性 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們一定是手工的 , 一起做點什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是反對女性 , 而是對我們、對我們女人、對我們的孩子來說 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我和暴力對抗 , 對抗恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校跟年輕的穆斯林女孩談話 , 這樣她們就不接受與她們的意志結婚了 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一位年輕女孩 , 並避免她們結婚 , 盡我所能地受苦 , 嗯 , 這是件好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是我在這裡的原因 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說我從aicha學到太多了 , 從那天開始 , 我們和其他家庭成員第一次開會 , 那是一個非常私密的會議 , 和安全的會議 , 因為那是2002年11月 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕那個時代的超級公平主義 , 那些我們家庭成員 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都非常緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 她為什麼想和我們見面 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	然後她很緊張 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 我們為什麼想見她 ? 」

before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們認識彼此的名字之前 , 或任何事之前 , 我們都曾經擁抱和編織過 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	然後我們坐在一個有支持、有幫助的圈子裡 , 從人們在這種和解中體驗到 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	aicha開始了 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是否有罪或無辜 , 但我想告訴各位 , 我對你的家庭造成了多麼遺憾 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道痛苦是什麼 , 我覺得如果有犯罪 , 一個人應該被公正審判 , 並受到懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她用那種方式向我們伸出援手 , 我想說 , 那是個冰箱 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的是 , 我們都說出自己的故事 , 我們都以人類的身分連結 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	在下午結束的時候----大概在午餐三小時後--我們會感覺到 , 彷彿我們永遠都知道對方 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的 , 是一位女性 , 不僅可以在現在的情況下如此慷慨 , 以及在她兒子身上做的事 , 還有她所擁有的人生 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過這麼辛苦的人 , 來自這樣的完全不同的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一個特別的連結 , 我非常重視 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我想這一切都是為了害怕對方 , 但讓那一步 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這並沒有那麼難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能遇到誰──我不知道 , 或那和我這麼不同 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , aicha , 你有幾個字可以做結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	aw:我想說我們必須試著認識他人 , 另一個人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須慷慨 , 而你的心一定是慷慨的 , 你的心靈一定是慷慨的 。

and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得這是來自一個安全的來源 。

what if it was from a source like this ?	如果是從這樣的來源呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	接著統計數字會說 , 你們當中有一半會患上腹瀉 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	我過去常常談到統計 , 以及所有人的安全飲用水 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但它們好像沒有穿過 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經搞懂了原因 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	是因為 , 用目前的思維 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法思考解決問題 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們直接關掉:我們 , 政府和援助機構 。

by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順帶一提 , 既然我一直在說話 , 全世界另外一萬三千人現在都在服用痢疾 。

i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifsaver濾水瓶 , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和你們一樣 , 坐下來 , 2004年聖誕節的那一天 , 我看著亞洲海嘯的毀滅性消息 , 在電視上播放 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	之後的日子和幾週 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝污染的水或面臨死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	那真的困在我身上 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	接著 , 幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風向美國的側邊滑了起來 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 , 」 我心想: 「 這是第一個世界國家 , 讓我們看看他們能做什麼 。 」

however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 在幾個失敗的原型之後 , 我終於想出了這個 , 救生員瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好了 , 現在為了科學的一點
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lifsaver之前 , 最好的手電過濾器只能過濾到大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約有200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以一個200奈米的細菌將會通過一個200奈米的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面最小的病毒則是大約25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以那絕對會穿過那200個奈米洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	救命saver的氣孔是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 沒有任何東西在穿越 。

traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?

the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題只會變得自我繁衍 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但用不同的方式思考 , 運送這些 , 人們可以留下來 。

using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	使用舊思維 , 國家基礎建設和管道工作 , 實在太貴了 。

instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水 , 使用人造流程來做 , 讓我們用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡取水 , 將水淡化 , 免費運送到那邊 , 然後把它丟到山上 , 河流 , 和溪流上 。

to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	若要把這點放到情境中 , 英國政府每年花約一百兩十億英鎊在外援助上 。

paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	paddown聲稱我們正生活在歷史上的一刻 , 權力從來沒有改變過它 。 在tedxbruss的演講中 , 他會把他所看到的三個重大的全球轉變推向 。

there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有首詩是十九世紀末一位非常著名的英文詩人寫的
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在1930年代 , 在邱吉爾的大腦中發出回音 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩說: 「 在夏天的冰山上 , 懶得帶著溪流的流動 , 哈克我聽到了一個遙遠的鼓聲 , 鼓聲就像是夢裡的聲音 , 距離又近又低又大聲 , 在地球的道路上 , 親愛的朋友和食物到粉末 , 士兵遊行 , 很快就要死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩感興趣的人 , 這首詩是 " shropshirelared " 由a.e.豪斯曼所寫 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但豪斯曼所理解的 , 你也在尼爾森交響曲中聽到的 , 是19世紀長、熱、絲毫的夏天 , 來到一個接近地點 , 我們即將進入一個歷史的恐怖時期 , 當權力改變時 , 我們即將進入一個歷史的恐怖時期 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	這些時期 , 各位先生女士 , 都伴隨著亂流 , 經常是血液 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我對你們的訊息是 , 我相信我們被譴責了 , 如果你願意 , 只活在歷史上的那些時刻之一 , 當那些權力被建立起來的權力開始改變 , 以及世界的新觀點 , 世界上存在的新勢力 , 已經開始形成 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	今天我們很清楚地看到 , 幾乎總是高度動盪的時代、高度困難的時光 , 通常都是非常血腥的時代 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	對了 , 每一世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會主張 , 上次發生的那段時間 , 休斯曼的感覺也來了 , 邱吉爾的感覺也是 , 當權力從舊國家通過 , 歐洲的舊勢力 , 橫跨大西洋 , 到大西洋的新興勢力 , 轉變為美國的新興勢力 , 美洲初期的起源 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 進入真空中 , 過去曾經有過太老的歐洲強權扮演了上個世紀的兩場血腥災難──第一部分和第二部分的兩場:兩場很棒的世界大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾將他們視為歐洲內戰 , 這可能是更精確的描述方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們住在其中一次 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天想談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	第一個 , 前兩個是關於權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個是關於一些我想要參考的新維度 , 這是從來沒有發生過的 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但我們來談談權力的轉變 , 發生在世界各地 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的是 , 在某種意義上 , 令人恐懼是因為從未發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經看到希臘的力量轉移到羅馬 , 以及發生在歐洲文明期間發生的權力轉移 , 但我們看到了稍微不同的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	對於權力 , 不只是稍微從國家轉移到國內 。
it's also moving vertically .	也是垂直移動的
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今發生的狀況是 , 被制定的權力 , 被責任 , 被告知 , 在國家國家的制度內 , 現在移到極大的衡量上 , 移到全球階段 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力全球化我們談到市場的全球化 , 但其實是真正的權力全球化 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級 , 權力是指責制定法律的 , 在國際舞台上也不是 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球舞台 , 現在有電源:網際網路的力量、衛星廣播的力量、金錢改變者的力量──這廣大的金錢改造者──現在流通了三十二倍──對貿易所需的金額──這應該是資金改變者 , 只要你喜歡 , 財務推論者將我們帶到我們的膝蓋 , 最近 , 跨國企業的力量 , 往往往往往往往比我國大的力量 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個極大的不受規範的全球空間裡 , 不受法律規範 , 而人們可能不受限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在那件衣服強大到一瞬間 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是適合那些在沒有限制的空間中運作最有權力的人 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 遲早 , 不受規範的空間空間不受限制 , 不只由你想要的國際貿易、網路 , 還有你不希望國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911事件的揭示是即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 那些居住空間的人 , 甚至可以在你最具代表性的城市中攻擊你 , 一個明亮的九月早晨 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 大約有60%被拿來資助9/11的400萬美金 , 實際上是通過雙胞胎塔的機構 , 其中9/11摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	要知道 , 我們的敵人也用這個空間-質量旅行、網路、衛星廣播者的空間 , 來到處走動他們的毒藥 , 也就是破壞我們的系統 , 以及我們的方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	遲早 , 或以後 , 歷史的規則是 , 權力統治的所在地必須遵守 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	因此 , 假如我相信 , 我們這個時代的一種現象就是權力全球化 , 那麼我們這個時代的挑戰就是將治理帶到全球空間 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信在我們面前的幾十年將會變成更大或更小的動亂--我們能達成那樣的目標:把治理帶到全球的空間 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	現在請注意 , 我不是在說政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是說設立一些全球民主制度
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順帶一提 , 女士們先生們 , 我自己的觀點是 , 這不太可能是由更多的聯合國機構推出的 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一種可以合法化國際行動的手段 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當涉及到全球空間的治理時 , 我的猜測是這樣的 , 不會透過更多的聯合國機構創造出來 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	它會發生在強而有力的聚集在一起 , 製造出基礎的系統 , 以條約為基礎的協議 , 來管理那個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到他們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:以約定為基礎的組織 , 完全以條約為基礎 , 然而 , 強大到足以包容即使是最強大的國家 , 美國 , 如果有必要的話 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	kyoto:掙扎的開始 , 創造一個以約定為基礎的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	g20:我們現在知道我們必須組成一個有能力將治理帶到金融空間的機構 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	而g20就是這樣 , 一個以約定為基礎的機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有一個問題 , 我們等一下會回來談這件事 , 那就是 , 如果你把最強大的團結結結起來 , 以條約為基礎的機構來做規則 , 來填補那個治理空間 , 那麼 , 留下的弱點會發生什麼事 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們只要一秒鐘就能回報它 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 如果你要在這些亂七八糟的時代中通過 , 那麼我們成功的做法 , 將取決於我們的能力 , 將合理的治理帶到全球的空間 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著那開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要和像這樣的觀眾談這樣的話 , 但權力不只是垂直轉移 , 同時也在橫向轉變 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會主張這個故事 , 文明的歷史 , 已被文明聚集在海上 , 和地中海附近的第一批人 , 在大西洋各地的西方勢力中 , 更近代的人聚集在一起 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在看到了一種基本的權力轉移 , 廣泛地說 , 遠離大西洋的國家聚集在大西洋 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這是從經濟力量開始的 , 但它總是這樣開始的 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增發生在世界上其他增長勢力的地區 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我覺得這不是西方國家的轉變 , 而是不同的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 值得的是 , 美國將保留地球上最強大的國家 , 在未來的十年、十五年 , 但她掌握權力的情境現在徹底改變了 , 徹底地改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們從50年來 , 最不尋常的歷史來到現在 , 我們有一個完全壟斷的世界 , 在每個羅盤針中 , 或反對的都要被它的位置給華盛頓一個由一個大腸桿菌所侵蝕的世界 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這不是歷史上常見的案例 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在出現的是更正常的歷史案例 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到一個多極化世界的出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直是我們這個世界的主導特色 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會維持最強大的國家 , 但他們會成為一個越來越多極化的世界中最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你開始看到在中國建立權力的替代中心 , 當然 , 我的猜想是 , 中國的財富不是平穩的 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	中國在解放經濟後 , 會很震撼 , 中國會開始民主化她的社會 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是不同的討論的主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	看到印度 , 看到巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到 , 現在的世界看起來 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 更像19世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	十九世紀的歐洲:一位偉大的英國外交部長 , 上任的罐頭 , 以前形容它是 「 歐洲音樂會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡 , 一個五分五的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是打到平衡點 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林結合 , 英國和維也納和羅馬結合 , 來提供反平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在一個由壟斷世界所主宰的時期 , 你已經修復了納托的盟友 , 也就是 「 戰爭鋸術 」 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	一個固定的權力對立意謂著固定的聯盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但 , 權力的多邊性 , 意味著移轉和改變聯盟 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們要進入的世界 , 我們將漸漸看到 , 我們的聯盟並不是固定的 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	坎寧 , 偉大的英國外交部長曾說: 「 英國有著共同的利益 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會逐漸發現 , 即使我們西方國家也會伸出援手 , 超越大西洋的舒適圈 , 來和其他人結盟 , 如果我們想讓世界各地的人都能做到 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 西方國家獨自做這件事是不夠好的 ; 我們得要讓其他人進去 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗是西方國家自己嘗試做這件事時的最後一次 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是 , 我們已經達到400年結束的開始--我說400年後--因為它是西方國家權力的熱門終結 , 西方制度和西方價值的終點 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道的 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家能一起行動 , 就能在世界各個角落提出和區分 。
but that's no longer true .	但那不再是事實 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以第二次世界大戰後最後的金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方結合了布雷頓森林機構 , 世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金解決了問題 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須在其他人打電話 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造g20
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須達到超越我們西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為你們做一個預測 , 這可能更令人驚訝 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們現在已經到了400年的終點 , 當時西方的權力已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國當然 , 他們永遠不會參與和平、跨國的和平活動 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	喔是嗎 ? 為什麼不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色的貝雷底下服役 , 在藍色旗下服役 , 在聯合國的指令下服役 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 11人 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	索馬利海盜的議題 , 最大的海盜內容是什麼 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國海軍的內容
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是商人國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想讓海道保持開放
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和那些我們不共享價值的人做生意 , 但 , 若要和誰共享價值 , 我們會分享共同利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的看法 , 現在正在興起的世界 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素是完全不同的 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天在我們的現代世界裡 , 因為網路 , 因為人們在這裡談論過的事物 , 一切都與萬物相連 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是相互依賴的
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	身為國家、個人 , 和以前從未有過的國家相互關聯 , 以前從來沒有這樣過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家之間的關聯性 , 嗯 , 總是存在的 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交是關於管理國家的關聯性 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們密切關在一起
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥得到豬流感 , 這是charlesdegaulle機場24小時後的問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟下降了 , 整個大量崩潰 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	在俄羅斯的步伐中有火災 , 非洲的糧食暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深、深刻、深深地相互連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	意思是 , 一個國家獨立行動的想法 , 與他人聯繫 , 而不是與他人合作 , 不再是可行的提議 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動都不受限制 , 也不足以讓國家自己掌控自己的領土 , 因為國家的影響已經開始影響他們內在的狀況 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是年輕的軍人 , 在英國最後一場小型帝國大戰中 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國的辯護是關於一件事 , 還有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強壯 , 我們的空軍有多強 , 我們的海軍有多強 , 以及我們的盟國有多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那是敵人在牆外的時候 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人在牆內
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想要談談我國家的防禦 , 我必須和健康部長談 , 因為流行疾病對我的安全是威脅 , 我必須和農業部長談談 , 因為糧食安全是對我的安全的威脅 , 我必須和工業部長談談 , 因為我們希地科技基礎設施的脆弱性 , 現在正是對我們的敵人的攻擊 , 正如同我們從網路戰場看到的目光 , 我得要和我的家務部長談談 , 因為他們在我國內已經進入了七個城市的威脅 , 因為他們在我國內部已經進入了 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	不再是國家的安全 , 對其士兵及其國防部而言 , 只是一件事 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	而是它的能力可以封鎖它的機構 。
and this tells you something very important .	這說明了一些非常重要的事
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建構 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式上垂直架構 , 專門處理任務的專門化 , 指令結構完全錯了 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	你在商業界知道我們這個時代的典範結構 , 各位先生女士 , 就是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	它是你有能力網絡的重要性 , 無論是你的政府內部 , 還是外部 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是ashdown的第三定律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順帶一提 , 不要問我關於shdown的第一個定律和第二個法則 , 因為我還沒發明這些法則 ; 如果有第三個法則 , 總聽起來更好 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	阿shown的第三定律是 , 在現代 , 所有東西都與萬物相連 , 最重要的是你能做的事 , 就是你能和他人做的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	關於你的結構 , 最重要的一點 , 不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍方的註冊 , 不論你是企業 , 都是你的夾克點 , 你的互助者 , 你和他人連結的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你明白在業界 , 政府沒有
but now one final thing .	但最後一件事情
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣 , 女士們先生們--也就是我們現在被關在一起--一種從來沒有相同的方式 , 那也是我們彼此之間的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 也是第一次 , 集體防禦 , 主導我們 , 保障我們的國家的概念 , 已經不夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我很安全 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我很安全 ; 我的同盟國 , 比如北托 , 比他們的同盟國更強大 , 我很安全 。
it is no longer the case .	不再是如此 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互關聯的進步 , 以及大規模破壞的武器 , 意味著 , 漸漸地 , 我和我的敵人分享了一個命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是外交官在1970年代與日內瓦的蘇聯協商時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們明白我們和他們分享了一個命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平已經來到北愛爾蘭因為雙方都意識到零和遊戲是行不通的
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們與敵人共享了一個命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東和平的大障礙之一 , 就是兩方 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦人 , 不了解他們共享集體命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	突然間 , 女士們先生們 , 什麼是 「 遠景者 」 和 「 詩人 」 的提議 , 變成我們必須認真看待公共政策的議題 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 我會用一首結束 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰唐妮的偉大詩
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要為誰送鐘 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是一座島嶼 。 」
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	它會說: 「 每個男人的死亡都影響著我 , 為了我參與人類 , 送我不要去要求誰的鐘聲 , 它會幫我做事 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對約翰唐恩來說 , 一個對道德的推薦
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 是我們生存的一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽和健康的路 , danbuettner和團隊研究全世界的 「 藍色區 」 , 他們的老年人和vigor住在一起 , 在tedxtc錄製時代 , 他共享了9個共通飲食和生活習慣 , 讓他們一直在100歲前流行 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物 , 文化 , 探索 , 食物 , 健康 , 生命 , 科學 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetner:如何活到100+ 。
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	所謂的丹麥雙胞胎研究指出 , 大約只有10%的平均壽命 , 在某些生物限制之內 , 是由我們的基因所主宰 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外90%是以我們的生活方式主宰的 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以 , 藍色區塊的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能想出一個長壽的事實公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問美國人 , 平均壽命的最佳公式是什麼 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南海灘的飲食 , 或是墨水飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食品金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們的是
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於真正幫助我們活得更久的事物 , 有許多困惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜珈嗎 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉還是吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	當談到補充物時 , 你是否該把它們
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	這些荷爾蒙還是反轉rol呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的是否在其中演奏 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神層面 ? 以及我們如何社交 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	嗯 , 我們找到長壽的方法是和國家地理雜誌合作 , 和國家老化研究所 , 找到四個人口統計的地區 , 來定義地理位置 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後帶一個專家團隊 , 去精確地經歷這些人所做的事 , 來提升跨文化的分歧 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴各位那句話是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先我想在長壽時緩解一些常見的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你真的很難活到100歲 ,
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 在美國 , 只有五千人中只有一人活到一百歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使是美國成長最快的人口統計數字 , 卻很難達到100 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是我們不是為了長壽而設計的 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們是為了一種叫 「 繁榮成功 」 的程式 。
i love that word .	我很喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起了我大學的日子
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 繁衍成功 」 , 意味著你有孩子的年齡 , 接著另一代 , 當你的孩子有孩子時 , 年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那演化的效果完全消失後 ,
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類 , 如果你是老鼠或大象 , 或人類 , 在兩者之間 , 都是一樣的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 若要讓它達到100歲 , 你不只需要有非常好的生活方式 , 你還得要贏得基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療可以幫助緩慢、反轉 , 或甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你想一想 , 有99件事情可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要幾分鐘 , 那些腦細胞就會死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球太硬 , 在膝蓋上 , 軟骨破壞 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用斑紋來連結 , 我們就能得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情要出錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 數萬億個 「 t 」 , 我們在這裡談的是國家債務數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每8年就會轉一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們轉向自己 , 就會造成一些損傷 。
and it builds up exponentially .	並且以指數型態建立
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像當時我們都有披頭四的專輯或老鷹專輯 , 我們會在錄音帶上做一份複製 , 讓朋友複製那錄音帶 , 很快地 , 我們就有了成功的世代 , 聽起來像垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	嗯 , 同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞身上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化速度大約是125倍 , 比一個12歲小孩還快 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有任何事情可以減緩老化或停止老化 , 我在這裡做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	事實是 , 最好的科學告訴我們人體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約有九十年 , 對女性來說 , 多一點點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這個國家的預期壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 沿著這條線的某處 , 我們在桌子上留下了大約12年的好年 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年我們可以得到的
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 大部份的慢性病、心臟病、癌症 , 和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要讓這些失落的年份最好的方法是去觀察世界各地的文化 , 實際上正在經歷的文化 , 那裡的人們活到100歲以上 , 比我們高出10倍 , 人口的壽命多出了十倍 , 而預期壽命的地區 , 中年死亡率是這個國家的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們在義大利海岸找到第一個藍色地帶 , 大約125英里外 , 在薩丁尼亞島上 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有140萬人 , 但只在高地上 , 一個叫做努羅省的地區 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡有一塊男人最長壽的地區 , 大約是美國這裡的百歲人數的十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不但達到一百歲 , 他們也用非凡的視覺來做 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	十二歲的老人仍騎腳踏車去上班 , 雜碎的木材 , 可以打敗一個比他們年輕60歲的人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史事實上回到了基督時期 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是被隔離的青銅時代文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是如此的富有 , 它們大多是牧羊人 , 這種情況是常規的、低密度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要是以植物為基礎的 , 用他們能帶進田裡的食物來集中 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一種未發酵的全麥麵包 , 叫做卡塔音樂麵包 , 用糞麥製成的一種乳酪 , 用草養殖的動物做成的一種乳酪 , 所以乳酪在omega-3脂肪酸中 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 來自玉米類型的脂肪酸 , 還有一種酒 , 比世界上任何已知葡萄酒的三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正的秘密在於他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	而薩丁尼亞社會中最常見的元素之一 , 就是他們對待老人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看看廣告
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞這裡 , 你越年紀越大 , 你就越有智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 與其看到運動說明游泳日曆 , 你看到月曆的百歲人 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 這不僅對你的老年父母有益 , 讓他們與家人保持距離 , 大約有四到六年的預期壽命研究顯示 , 對那些家庭的孩童來說 , 死亡率和疾病的比例也比較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	也就是所謂的祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一端發現了我們的第二個藍色區域 , 位在東京南邊 , 位於俄國的亞基拉哥南邊 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而在主島的北部 , 這是世界長壽的第零度 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這個地方是最古老的女性族群找到的 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	在這個地方 , 人們擁有世上最長的殘障壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們的睡眠時間很長 , 通常很快就會死去 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 性愛之後 ,
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們的壽命大約比美國平均長七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	和我們在美國有五倍的百歲人一樣 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	第五名殖民和乳癌的比率 , 美國這裡的大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	以及心血管疾病的六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	而這個文化已經產出了這些數字 , 暗示他們有東西可以教我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 一個以植物為基礎的飲食 , 裡面有許多顏色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	而他們和美國人一樣吃大約八倍的豆腐 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的東西更顯著 , 就是他們如何吃它 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略可以避免過量 , 如你所知 , 這是美國的一個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們所觀察到的一些策略:它們會從較小的盤子裡吃掉 , 所以它們會在每個座落時吃比較少的卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其服務家庭風格 , 你可以在談話時無意地吃飯 , 他們在櫃檯服務 , 把食物放走 , 然後帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有一個3000歲的小孩 , 我覺得這是有史以來最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	是由confcius發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食被稱為 「 騷擾、哈奇、野生飲食 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	這只是一個小小的說法 , 這些人在他們吃飯之前 , 提醒他們 , 當他們的胃有80%時 , 停止進食 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	這種感覺大概需要半小時 , 才能從肚子傳到大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	請記住 , 80%的協助是讓你不去做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 像薩丁尼亞 , okinawa有一些社交建構可以和長壽相關 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會殺人 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 美國人平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在已經下降到一半了
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你幸運地出生在琉球 , 你出生在一個系統中 , 你自動擁有一半十多個朋友 , 和你一輩子一起旅行的人 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為moai 。 如果你在moai你會被期待分享彈跳如果你遇到幸運的話 , 如果事情不好的話 , 孩子會生病 , 家長就會死去 , 你總是會有一個有你的背心的人 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這位特別的摩艾 , 這五位女士已經在一起了97年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國我們把成人生活分為兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	還有我們的工作生活 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 砰 , 我們退休了
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這意味著退休到簡單的椅子上 , 或是下到亞利桑那州去打高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在okinawan的語言中 , 連退休的詞語都沒有 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是 , 一生中有一個字 , 那個字就是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大概翻譯一下 , 意思是 「 你早上醒來的理由 。 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這位102歲的凱特大師而言 , 他的ikigai是為了這場戰火藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這百歲的漁民而言 , 每週要捕魚三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 , 國家老化研究院給了我們一份問卷 , 給了這些百歲人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們非常文化上是那些放問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上起床
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位102歲的老女人來說 , 她的ikigai只是她的曾曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101歲半時分離 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 抱著一個曾曾曾曾曾曾孫女的感覺是什麼 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把頭放回去 , 說: 「 感覺就像跳進天堂一樣 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我以為那是個美好的思想 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理雜誌的編輯希望我能找到美國的藍色區 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子我們探討明尼蘇達的禱告 , 實際上有非常高比例的百歲人 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有年輕人留下的
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再次轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國長壽的人口 , 在加州的羅馬林達和加州的羅馬林達 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	冒險家是保守主義者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五從日落到日落的日落慶祝他們的安息日 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	一個時間的24小時聖所 , 他們稱之為
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 傳達給他們非凡的長壽 , 相對來說 ,
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 對一般女性來說 , 平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一位冒險女士來說 , 他們的預期壽命是89
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	不同之處在於男性間的發音 , 她們期待比她們的美國人多活11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	現在 , 這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林研究 。 我覺得它最適合說明了這個藍色區計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異族族群 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共通點是一組非常小的生活習慣 , 以儀式的方式遵循他們大部分的人生 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	直接從聖經中奪走他們的飲食
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	基因:第29章 , 上帝在哪裡談到umumes和種子 , 在另一個關於綠色植物的史丹扎上 , 根本缺少的就是肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真看待這個庇護所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論他們有多忙碌 , 工作上有多大壓力 , 孩子需要被驅逐 , 他們停止一切 , 專注在他們的上帝 , 他們的社交網路 , 接著 , 堅守在宗教中 , 大自然是行走的 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這方面的力量並不是偶爾完成的 , 權力是它每週一次完成一次 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	都不難 , 不用花錢
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒險家也傾向和其他冒險家在一起 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個冒險家的派對 , 你不會看到有人在搖晃吉姆樑 , 或滾動一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	他們反而在談論他們的下一生走路、交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們會祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們以深刻且可測量的方式互相影響 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化已經產出了ellswrehareham
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	ellswhareham是97歲
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是個多百萬富翁 , 但當一個承包商想要6 , 000美金來建造一個隱私柵欄時 , 他說: 「 為了這類的錢我自己來做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天 , 他就在外面衝擊水泥 , 四處拖著北極 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可預料的是 , 也許到了第四天 , 他最後到了手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是當桌上的那個人 ; 那個人做開心手術 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	在97年 , 他仍然每個月進行二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•波林斯 , 103歲 , 現在 , 一隻活躍的牛仔 , 早上開始他的游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	週末他喜歡裝在板子上 , 丟棄羅斯特尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在這兒的雙胞胎城市 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從抬重的日子開始 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	然後她到她的根部 , 1994年的cadidiacseville , 撕下了聖伯納多高速公路 , 在那裡 , 她仍然有七個不同組織的志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我已經進行了19次硬體探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是唯一一個你遇過的人 , 他騎腳踏車穿越撒哈拉沙漠 , 卻沒有防曬霜的人 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴你們 , 沒有任何冒險比起騎馬爾吉•戴頓搭乘的火車更為傷害 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 一個陌生人是我還沒見面的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說:
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那麼 , 這三種文化中的常識是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都做了什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功地將它歸結為9 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們從此以後 , 做了兩個藍色地帶探險 , 這些共同的探險家持有真實的立場 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	第一個 , 我即將要在這裡演講 , 沒有一個運動 , 至少我們認為運動的方式是如此 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們設立自己的生命 , 以便他們不斷地被推進到實體活動中 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這百歲的琉球婦女正起身離開地面 , 每天30或40次坐在地上 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子 , 上下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店、教堂 , 或去朋友家 , 偶爾會走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何方便 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有按鈕來做院子的工作或房屋工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想混合一個蛋糕 , 他們就用手去做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	那燃燒卡路里的熱量和跑步機一樣多 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做故意的身體活動時 , 他們很享受的東西 。 他們傾向於走路 , 唯一證實的方法是脫離認知的衰退 , 他們都傾向擁有一個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式來建立他們的生活 , 這樣他們才有正確的外觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間來下班 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 七天的冒險家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawans有這個祖先的神經
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你處在傷口或壓力之中時 , 會觸發所謂的發炎反應 , 這和所有東西有關 , 從阿茲海默症到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你一天放慢十五分鐘 , 你將那發炎狀態變成更抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們的詞彙是有目的、ikigai , 像琉球人一樣 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 而你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的目的感 , 並且在他們的生活中啟動 , 這價值約七年的額外壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反的 , 這些人每天喝一點 , 而不是賣給美國人口的難度 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們傾向吃以植物為基礎的飲食
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不代表他們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆子和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	而且他們有一些策略可以避免過分過量 , 那些在對的時間把他們推離桌子的小東西 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	接著 , 這一切的基礎是他們如何聯繫 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們先放家人 , 照顧他們的孩子和老化父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向屬於一個以信仰為基礎的社群 , 值四到十四年的預期壽命 , 如果你每個月做四次的話 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	而這裡最大的是他們也屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是出生就是積極地圍繞著自己 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從franmingham研究中得知 , 如果你的三個最好的朋友是肥胖的 , 有50%的機會是過重的 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人在一起 , 那會隨著時間產生可測量的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你朋友的休閒想法是身體活動 , 保齡球 , 或玩曲棍球 , 騎腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點點 , 但不多 , 他們吃得對 , 他們也很投入 , 他們信任、值得信任 , 這將會隨著時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食不可行 , 世界上的飲食史上沒有用過超過2%的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計劃通常從一月開始 ; 它們通常是十月完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當談到 「 長壽 」 時 , 在藥丸或其他任何方面都沒有 「 短期修復 」 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你想一想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許是你能做的最重大的事 , 為你的生活增加更多年 , 多謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水導電 ; 一扇窗 , 從輕而易舉的開關轉向不透明 ; 一個讓音樂的水母 。 所有這些東西都存在 。 卡塔琳娜•莫塔塔說:是時候來玩它 。 莫塔引領我們踏上驚喜和酷炫的新材料 , 建議我們找出它們最適合的辦法 , 就是實驗、水槽和有趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力 , 設計 , 科技 ,
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩弄智慧材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一個在葡萄牙的朋友 , 他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機建造了一台車 , 這樣他就可以運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他負擔不起車子 , 也因為他知道如何建造一個 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	有段時間 , 我們了解事物是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何製造的 , 這樣我們就可以建造和修復它們 , 或最不具體的決定 , 關於要購買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多這種做法在20世紀後半葉失去了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者社群和開放原始碼模型 , 帶給我們這種知識 , 關於事物如何運作 , 以及它們在我們的生活中所構成的知識 , 我相信我們需要帶它們到下一個層面 , 帶到物品組成的成分 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的部分 , 我們仍然知道紙張和紡織品的傳統材料是由什麼組成的 , 以及它們是如何生產的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些驚人又具功率的複合材料 , 能改變形狀、油漆 , 能導電、顏料 , 會改變顏色、會發光的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電油墨讓我們可以塗上電路 , 而不是使用傳統印刷電路板或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我握住的這個小例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個觸碰感測器 , 藉由打開這個小小的光來反應我的皮膚 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	導電油墨已經被藝術家使用 , 但近期的開發指出 , 我們很快就能用雷射印表機和筆 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這張紙上放著無色光線散射的粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	意思是 , 當普通的水晶體只在邊緣散射光線時 , 這個會照亮整個表面 , 當我打開它周圍的光線時 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這材料的兩種應用包括內部設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	而熱變色顏料會在特定溫度上改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個放在熱盤上 , 溫度只比野生高一點點 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這種材料的其中一個原理就是 , 在其他東西中 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 它指出 , 當內容物夠酷 , 可以喝 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一般所謂的智慧型材料的幾個 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	在幾年內 , 它們會在我們每天使用的許多物品和技術中 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有讓飛行車科幻小說對我們保證 , 但我們能有牆壁 , 根據溫度、按鍵板來改變顏色的顏色 , 會捲起來 , 窗戶會在開關的瞬間變成不透明 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是一名社會科學家 , 所以 , 為什麼我今天在這裡談論智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事物如何運作 , 以及如何製造 , 也因為我相信我們應該要更深入了解構成我們世界的組成部分 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技的複合物了解不足──我們的未來將由此組成 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧材料很難在小量中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	在如何使用它們上幾乎沒有任何資訊 , 非常少有人說它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 它們主要存在於貿易秘密和專利的領域 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	所以 , 三年前 , 克雷斯泰.男孩和我開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 開放材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是我們這個網站 , 任何其他人想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗、發表資訊 , 鼓勵其他人在任何時候能做出貢獻 , 並集結資源 , 例如研究論文和教學 , 由其他像我們一樣的製造者來做 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個大型、集體產生的資料庫 , 用智慧材料來做資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但為什麼我們要關心智慧材料如何運作 , 以及它們是由什麼組成的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們不能塑造我們不了解的東西 , 以及我們不了解和使用的東西 , 最後會塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們所使用的物品 , 我們所穿的衣服 , 我們所居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要生活在一個由智慧材料構成的世界 , 我們應該要知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	其次 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新一直都被tinker公司燃料到 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘者 , 不是專家 , 都是從山腳到半導體、個人電腦、飛機的發明家和改良者 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學很複雜 , 且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但並非總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾州大學的兩位科學家了解這一點 , 他們發表了一篇論文 , 用比較簡單的方法來製作導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	約旦bunker , 他對化學沒有經驗 , 直到那時 , 讀了這篇論文 , 並在他的製造者空間中繁衍出實驗 , 只用外衣的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至做了自己的vorex混合器 , 根據另一位科學家/maker的課輔 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦在網路上發表了他的研究結果 , 包括所有他曾經嘗試過、沒有用的東西 , 讓其他人可以研究和複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 約旦的主要創新形式是把一個在大學創造的完善裝備實驗室的實驗 , 並在芝加哥的車庫中重現它 , 只用便宜的材料和工具 , 讓他成為自己 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他發表了這個作品 , 其他人可以拿起他離開的地方 , 設計出更簡單的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個例子我想提一下她的專案目標是要強調材料的表達特質同時著重於建築者的創意和技能
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備在其中非常強大 , 它們教導我們事情如何運作 , 但在它們的設計中 , 內在的限制影響了我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , 漢娜的做法是建立一系列的技巧 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 讓我們不受預先設計的限制 , 透過教導我們關於材料本身的知識 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個實驗 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面有一些銅製膠帶連接到mp3播放器和磁鐵
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	基於麻省理工學院的marcelocoelho所做的研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅膠帶到導電布料和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和其他許多製造者 , 漢娜發表了她的食譜 , 讓任何人都能複製和繁衍 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙本電子產品是最有前景的材料科學分支之一 , 它讓我們能創造出更便宜又有彈性的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的工藝作品 , 以及她分享她的發現的事實 , 將門打開 , 讓一連串新的可能性 , 都是美學上吸引和創新的 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造家有趣的地方在於 , 我們創造出熱情和好奇心 , 我們並不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從不傳統的角度去處理問題 , 在這個過程中 , 最後發現了替代方案 , 或甚至更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以越多人用材料做實驗 , 研究人員就越願意分享他們的研究 , 製造商他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正服務我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以 , 我覺得有點像tednelson在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在一定懂電腦了 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	在那時 , 電腦是這些大型的主體只有科學家在乎 , 甚至沒有人夢想在家裡有一台 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你現在一定要了解智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 關於新興科技的先入為主的知識是確保我們在未來有個說法的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入一個玻璃泡 , 鎖上門 , 按下加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛來引導我們 , 即使我們只能看到前面和後面幾輛車 。 但是 , 如果車子能彼此分享資料 , 關於它們的位置和速度 , 並用預測模型來計算路上的每個人最安全路線 ? 珍妮佛能想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	jenniferhealey:如果汽車可以說話 , 意外可能是可以避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧:開車是危險的
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的其中一件事 , 但宗教標誌和好運魅力卻出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛了我們所知道的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國16到19歲的人的主要死因 , 導致死亡的原因 , 其中75%的意外與毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定說 , 但我記得我的第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我在高速公路上是個年輕的駕駛員 , 前面的車子 , 我看到煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙慢了下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停了下來 , 死了 , 死在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只剩65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我撞上煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我覺得abs打進去了 , 車子還在走 , 也不會停下來 , 我知道不會停下來 , 空袋部署 , 車子已經完全安排了 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道車子停了 , 我想我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以透過讓我們的車子彼此交談來改變駕駛經驗 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只想讓各位稍微思考一下開車是什麼樣的體驗 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車裡 , 關上門 。 你在一個玻璃泡裡 ,
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你真的無法直接感知你周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是將它往下導入部分的路徑 , 進入和其他金屬巨人之間 , 以超人的速度進行導航 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要引導你是你的兩個眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好的 , 這就是你所擁有的 , 眼睛並不是為了這個任務而設計的 , 但後來人們會要求你做一些事 , 像是 , 你想要做一個車道變換 , 他們問你的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上取下 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	不要看你要去哪裡 , 轉向 , 檢查你的盲點 , 然後開車到不看你要去的地方 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是開車的安全方法 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做一個選擇 , 我要看這裡還是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做很棒的工作挑選 , 選擇我們在路上所參加的一切 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會錯過一些事情 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會感覺到錯或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這點 , 我相信
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看這麼多
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在的科技可以幫助我們改善它 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	未來 , 車子彼此交換資料 , 我們將能看到不只是三部車前進 , 還有三部車 , 往後移動 , 向右和左 , 全部同時 , 鳥的眼睛觀點 , 我們真的能夠看到這些車 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能夠看到前面車輛的速度 , 看看那傢伙走得多快 , 或停下多快 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那傢伙下降到零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	藉由計算和演算法和預測模型 , 我們將能夠看見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能覺得這不可能
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你怎麼能預測未來 ? 那真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 沒有 。 用汽車 , 不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車子是三維的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們沿著道路行駛 ,
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們在出版的路線上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要做出合理的預測並不難在不久的將來
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	就算 , 當你在車裡 , 有些摩托車騎士來了 , 每小時85英里的車程下來 , 車道平盤 , 我知道你有過這個經驗 , 那個人沒有 「 只是從無處走出來 。 」
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙在路上大概在過去的半小時
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10 , 20 , 30英里後面 , 有人看到那傢伙 , 一輛車看到那個傢伙 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他位置、速度、好估計 , 他會以每小時85英哩的速度持續下去 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為另一輛車會在他耳邊竊竊取一些東西 , 比如: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 看看 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以對汽車的行為做出合理的預測
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是牛頓物品 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	那我們要如何達到目標呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 如分享我們在車之間的位置資料 , 只要分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我車子裡有一台gps和攝影機 , 我很精確地知道我在哪裡 , 以及我要多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我周圍的車子在哪裡 , 有點像是他們要去哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確地了解他們所處的位置 , 並且有點模糊地想出其他車子的位置 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩部車彼此分享這些資料 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以完全告訴你會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊已經做了電腦模擬 , 模擬當模擬模擬結果 , 當模擬混合器結合時 , 甚至在輕型交通中 , 當汽車共享gps資料時 , 我們把這項研究移到電腦模擬中 , 進入機器人檢測床 , 有實際的感測器 , 在這些機器人身上:音響相機、gps , 以及二維雷射級的發現者 , 這些在後備系統中很常見的發現者 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也附上了一段距離短距的通訊電台 , 機器人彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人彼此相處時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們可以避開彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在把越來越多的機器人加入混合當中 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你收到太多的聊天時 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你必須優先處理 , 那就是預測模型協助你的地方 。
