if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人汽車都在追蹤預期的軌跡 , 你不會注意那些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	優先順序這個傢伙看來有點不順利 。
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能會是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	並且可以預測新軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他會走路 , 你知道怎麼走 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而你也知道你需要警告哪個司機出門 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	而我們想怎麼做才能警告每一個人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車怎麼能低聲說: 「 你需要走出路來 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:第一 , 汽車的能力 , 以及第二種驅動力的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有一個人擁有一台很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 你知道的 , 做一些事 , 他們不可能會在緊急狀況中做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了一項分開的研究 , 進行駕駛狀態模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用一系列的三部攝影機 , 我們可以偵測到 , 如果一個司機向前看 , 向下看 , 在電話上看 , 或是拿著一杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外 , 我們可以預測誰 , 哪一輛車是最好的位置 , 要搬出最安全的路線 , 才能計算出每個人最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術現今存在 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為 , 我們面臨最大的問題是我們自己的意願分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我覺得這是個非常令人不解的概念 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 談論我們到其他車 , 我們會在一片八卦的大海中往下走 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信可以用一種方式保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在一樣 , 當我從外面看你的車時 , 我不太清楚你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看著你的車牌號碼 , 我真的不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車可以在背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	而我認為這會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	請各位考慮一下 , 如果你真的不想要後面的青少年 , 知道你在煞車 , 你要來到死胡同 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過分享我們的資料願意 , 我們能為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車八卦談談你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	會讓道路變得更安全
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize創辦人peterdiamandis談到他如何幫助stephenhawking實現了他的夢想 , 藉由一起飛進上層大氣層 , 並在0g中體驗無重量 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短談、太空、科技、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	peterdiamandis在stephenhawking在zerogrohawking
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	那些認識我的人知道我對打開太空前線有多熱情 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給世界的專家重力--無重力的體驗 , 這真是太不可思議了 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴你們那個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他 , 透過基因組學獎 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的一個競賽 , 第二個xprize , 給第一個在10天內完成100個人類基因組定序的團隊 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的基因組-100個個個體--我們將其定序為一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特椅子那事件
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是要到太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到那裡 , 但我可以帶你進入無重力進入零度 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他回答: 「 沒錯 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 要在地球上體驗無重力飛行的唯一方法 , 其實是用雙重飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	搭飛機 , 飛越頂端 , 體重不重25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再回來 , 你的重量是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再再而三地
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8 , 10分鐘的無重力 , 美國太空總署如何訓練他們的太空人這麼久 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始做這件事 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣佈要飛史蒂芬•霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機關 , 一間公司飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 不要這樣做 , 你要殺那個人 。
and he wanted to go .	而他想去
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下來 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們舉辦了一場媒體大會 , 我們宣佈我們的意圖是要做一個零的拋物線 , 給他25秒的0 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果真的很順利 , 我們可能會做三個拋物線 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他為什麼想上去做這件事
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他所說的 , 對我來說 , 非常動人 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命正面臨著被災難摧毀的危機......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為人類的種族沒有未來 , 如果沒有進入太空的話 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此 , 我想要鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們把他帶到甘迺迪太空中心 , 帶到太空總署車內 , 進入零和飛機的後方 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們大約有20個人捐款 , 我們捐出150 , 000美元捐款給和我們一起飛行的兒童慈善機構 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個tedster
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了整顆er 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四位急診室醫生和兩位護士登上飛機 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監測他的血液 , 他的心跳加速 , 他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	一切都發生在緊急狀況下 , 天曉得 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落設施起飛 , 太空梭起飛 , 降落的地方 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	而我的另一半mronlichtenberg和我很小心地把他暫停成零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他到了那裡 , 讓他去體驗無重力是真正的樣子 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在第一個拋物線之後 , 你知道的 , 醫生說一切都很棒 , 他微笑 , 我們說:
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們實際上向艾薩克牛頓爵士致敬一個蘋果 , 因為霍金教授在牛頓大學舉辦了同樣的椅子 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四、第五、第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	和第七和第八個 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像個65歲的輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在一個珍貴的珠寶上 , 在我們有生之年 , 我們正在離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請在這個史詩冒險中加入我們 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫家davidbolinsky呈現了三分鐘的驚人動畫 , 顯示在一個細胞內的緊繃生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、科技、視覺化 ,
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插圖家 , 我從稍微不同的角度
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在看 , 自從我長大以來 , 在藝術中 , 真與美的表達 , 以及科學中的真與美 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這兩樣都是美好的事物 , 但它們都有美好的事物 , 真相和美 , 可以被科學和數學看待的理想 , 幾乎就像是科學家想要約會的理想對象中的雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達真理是令人敬畏的事物 , 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是有力的理想 , 它們是不可思議的
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 , 有時是有用的 , 通常在事實之後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以翻一些照片 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美是那些經常對科學不在的人不在乎的事物 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用一種方式描述美麗的事物 , 它通常只能用一種方式 , 只要你了解這個語言 , 以及研究這個主題的人 , 在哪一個真相和美所表現出來的 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看看宇宙的常數 , 那裡有一個人類的理想 , 在那裡 , 你可以看到生命必須從描述宇宙的數字演化出來 , 這些都是很難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被教導為醫學插圖師以來 , 我一直試著要做的是 , 我父親教導我的動畫 , 他是雕塑家和我的視覺導師 , 我想要想出一種方式 , 來幫助人們了解生物科學中的真與美 , 透過動畫 , 通過圖片 , 說明故事 , 如此一來 , 人們不見得能被帶到的東西 , 可以被帶到它 , 且能被教導 , 並且能夠被了解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生常常會沉浸在一個環境中 , 學習的是有真與美的主題 , 包含在他們身上 , 但他們被教導的方式是相對的 , 且它被吸引到 , 直到真相和美是不見得總是顯而易見的地方 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	幾乎就像是雞湯的舊食譜 , 在那裡煮雞肉 , 直到香味不見了 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對學生這樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我在哈佛的robertlue打電話給哈佛的分子和細胞生物學部門 , 幾年前 , 他問我和我的團隊是否有興趣 , 願意真正改變哈佛的醫學和科學教育 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始了一項計畫 , 探索細胞的真與美 , 探索分子和細胞生物學的真相與美 , 讓學生可以了解一個更大的圖片 , 讓他們可以把這些事實都掛在上面 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可能有一套牢房的心智圖像 , 一個龐大的 , 巨大的複雜的城市 , 被微機械佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	而這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 就是奈米科技專家的羨慕 , 都是自主、強大、精確、精確、精確的裝置 , 都是用氨基酸做的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	而這些微機械驅動細胞如何移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們會影響細胞如何複製 。 它們會影響我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	它們能影響我們的心靈 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以 , 我們想要做的是 , 把這個故事變成一個動畫 , 成為哈佛的生物分析中心 , 一個哈佛大學的生物分析中心 , 一個哈佛的網站 , 為它的分子和細胞生物學的學生 , 除了所有文字資訊之外 , 所有大量文字的東西 , 把所有東西都放在一起 , 讓這些學生對細胞真正的真相和美 , 能夠用這個觀點來研究它們的觀點 , 讓它們的想像力被激發出來 , 讓它們能夠被發現 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是 , 你有巨噬細胞 , 讓它流下毛細管 , 它們在碰觸毛細管壁的表面 , 它們從毛細管壁上撿起資訊 , 它們被賦予了這些資訊 , 外面有一個發炎 , 在那裡 , 在那裡 , 它們看不到和感覺 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到引導他們停止的資訊 , 引導他們內化 , 認為他們需要製造出所有會造成他們改變形狀的各個部分 , 試圖脫離這個毛細管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須與哈佛的科學家及原子準確分子的資料清晰模型合作找出它們是如何移動的然後找出它們是如何移動的
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想出如何用真相的方式來做這件事 , 實情實在在太實在了 , 但不太實在 , 牢房裡的擁擠會阻止這次發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	所以我要給你們看的是一部三分鐘的讀者消化這部電影的第一個面向這是一個持續進行的專案計畫將在四、五年後再進行一次
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請大家看看這段影片 , 看看細胞製造這些小小的行走機器的路徑 , 它們被稱為kines , 將這些巨大的負載載量 , 以相對尺寸挑戰螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	播放電影 , 拜託 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器真的很了不起 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	將資訊傳遞給彼此 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成不同的事情發生在細胞內 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造它在果蠅上需要的部分 , 從從從讀取基因的分子所帶來的細胞核中得到的資訊 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每個人 , 都有可能沒有這些微機械 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 克里斯的出席率非常高 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的聯邦快遞人員 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做kinesin , 他拉著一個裝滿全新的製造蛋白質的尖端 , 到細胞中不管是需要在哪裡 , 不論是用來做薄膜 , 不論是用來製造或修復某樣東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人大約有十萬個這種東西跑來跑去 , 目前 , 每一百兆個細胞中就有十萬個 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多懶惰 , 你都沒有做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 當你回家時 , 我要你做的是想想這個 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想我們在學習細胞機械的一些東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞清楚這一切 , 相信我 , 我們幾乎知道一旦搞清楚到底發生了什麼事 , 我們真的能夠掌握許多控制權 , 控制我們的健康 , 帶著我們在未來的世代 , 以及我們活了多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用這個方法來發現更多的真相 , 還有更多的美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但非常驚人的是這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 已經足夠意識到它們所需要的細胞到底是什麼 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們一起工作 。 它們讓細胞做它需要做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起合作幫助我們體內巨大的實體 , 他們永遠看不到正常的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受其餘的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝基•布蘭頓計畫要在她的車子裡住一整年 , 看看這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症進入 , 她的自由工作結束時 , 她的營地旅行轉變成無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她成為無家可歸的體驗 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、說故事、說故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝基•布蘭頓:那年我無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是個作家和記者 , 我也是一個瘋狂好奇的人 , 所以 , 在22年裡 , 身為記者 , 我學會了如何做很多新事 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學會了一件事 , 就是變得隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為了無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭掉我身為報紙編輯的工作 , 在我父親在同一年二月去世後 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死感打了我 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我做這件事的時候 , 有很多我想要去感受和處理的事 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一輩子都露營了 。 我決定活在一輛車上 , 要做這件事就好像一趟漫長的露營旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我打包我的貓 , 我的鹿威爾和我的露營裝備 , 進入1975年的雪佛蘭車中 , 開車進入日落 , 完全沒能實現三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	一:那個社會是以永久結構生活的 , 甚至是以一個人的價值為基礎 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	二:我沒有意識到別人的負面看法有多快會影響我們的現實 , 如果我們讓它 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒有意識到 , 無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在車裡很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 , 定期吃完
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	而我還有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接下來我父親死後的憤怒和沮喪
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 我得要找全職的工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	一個非常溫和的春天 , 變成了極熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	在任何地方都不可能停車 , 不用很明顯地我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 穿過了車子裡的開窗 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗進入了護理日 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能用員工淋浴在辦公大樓和卡車站
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或在公共場所洗衣服
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間車內溫度很少在華氏80度以下降低 , 讓很難或不可能睡覺 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中腐爛
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰塊裡的冰層數小時內就融化了 , 非常悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起找一間公寓 , 或負擔不起一間公寓 , 讓我有了腐爛者和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我待在車子裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱能讓我太病了 , 走到我晚上車外的公共廁所五十英尺外 , 我用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天到冬天時 , 溫度低於冰凍 。 他們待在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	而我面對了全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上停車不一樣的地方 , 以避免被警察察察察察察察 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我覺得我無法掌控我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時或如何發生 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者 , 變成一個無家可歸的女人 , 住在車子裡 , 把我的呼吸帶走 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 , 我的智商沒有下降 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的天份、我的正直、我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的事情都保持一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我在某種程度上改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我越深入陷入憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人提到我參加了一個遊民健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	然後我去了 。 我三天沒洗澡 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊中的任何人一樣感到沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒有喝醉或高喝酒 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當幾個無家可歸的男人意識到 , 包括一個前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸者 。 你為什麼會在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人並沒有把我視為無家可歸 , 但我做到了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著教授聽了我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	對藥物的反應讓我有自殺傾向 。 我記得: 「 如果我自殺 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	在那之後沒多久 , 一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆.羅斯特 , 一位全國知名的記者 , 一直在全國性電視台上談論我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	一篇我寫的文章 , 是他死前的那一年 , 在提姆的新書上 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在做演講迴路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到timrusert , 《見面新聞》的前主持人在談論我的寫作 , 當我住在華爾瑪停車場的一輛車裡 , 我開始笑了 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 是因為它到達了重點 , 我是作家 , 還是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我在書店找到提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	然後我就站在那裡 , 把我的文章重新上去 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久我搬回了田納西州
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友住在車子裡 , 和沙發衝浪之間 。
and i started writing again .	然後我又開始寫作
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	到了隔年夏天 , 我是個工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得獎項 。 我住在自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再是無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	而我不再隱形 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人工作完整且兼職工作 , 住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續汙名化、犯罪化 , 生活在你的車輛或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以無家可歸 , 工作無家可歸 , 主要是保持隱形 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你曾經碰過一個 , 讓他們參與 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何事情 , 如果有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡當海報的女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵你們把錢給你遇到的隔壁乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是住在哪裡 , 睡在哪裡 , 或任何時候的生活狀況是什麼 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前我住在沃爾瑪汽車停車場的一輛車 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是 , 總是找到一個方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxange , 泰國的《保險套先生》mechaiviravaida , 帶我們走過全國的大膽計劃 , 來提高生活水準 , 從1970年代開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著很多法蘭克 , 很有趣 , 且非常有效地談論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	mechaiviravaidya:保險套先生如何讓泰國變得更好 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	40年前當我還是個年輕人的時候 , 這個國家非常貧窮 , 很多很多生活在貧窮中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定為此做點什麼 , 但我們並沒有從福利計畫開始 , 或減少貧窮計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭開展計畫開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的母子健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭規劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有生存下去 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:來到孩子們 , 到媽媽們身邊 , 然後跟著家計劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是孩童死亡率 , 你也需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回來談為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的情況 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每百分之七的孩童 , 成長率是3.3 。
there was just no future .	只是沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女人說: 「 我們會同意 。 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要一個醫生來開藥 。 」 而我們只有非常少數的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有把答案當作答案 ; 我們不去問這個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去看護士和中產階級 , 他們也是女性 , 做了很棒的工作 , 來解釋如何使用藥丸 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那真是太棒了 , 但只涵蓋了全國的20% 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為另外80%的人留下了什麼 , 說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去找你看到的普通人
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	事實上 , 在那個黃色標誌下--我希望他們還沒把這個字擦掉 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	我們當時比可口可樂大得多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的人就是我們選的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很有名 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們很棒 , 他們自己練習家庭計劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地供應藥丸和保險套 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以我們去找那些被視為問題的原因的人 , 來解決問題 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論在哪裡 , 各位都能看到船上有女性 , 這裡賣的就是漂浮市場販售香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕藥 , 不論你在哪裡找到人 , 你會在泰國找到避孕藥 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	接著 , 我們決定 , 為什麼不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會很強壯 , 泰國人是佛教徒 。

we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年介紹了我們第一個小額貸款計畫 , 整理了這個計畫的婦女說: 「 我們只想借給實踐家庭規劃的婦女 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你不懷孕 , 你可以從我們那裡取出貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是他們經營的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	過了35/36年 , 還在進行中 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真正的銀行 , 而是基金小額貸款 。

because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能 , 也缺乏功勞 。

we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳創業家 , 小生意人

and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮中的人 , 能取得信用一定是人權 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能感覺像是朋友 , 但真的朋友會在一陣子給你微笑 。 在ted2013年 , 凱勒•里納多•德摩多 , 智慧型手機驅動的迷你機器人 , 他可以在散步上和你一起運動 , 滑動你一杯咖啡 , 用可程式化的表達方式對你做出反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個由你的手機供電的迷你機器人 。

that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們在romotive公司試圖解決的問題我和其他20位在romotive的書呆子都迷上了解決問題
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想建造一個任何人都可以使用的機器人 , 不論你是8或80歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是個很困難的問題 , 因為你必須建立一個小型、可攜帶的機器人 , 不僅僅是真正負擔得起的 , 它還必須是人們真正想要帶回家 , 帶著他們的孩子到處走 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人無法令人毛骨悚然或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該很友善和可愛 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個機器人 , 用你已經知道的裝置 , 愛你的iphone作為他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由iphone的處理器發揮力量 , 我們可以創造一個機器人 , 它能讓一百五十美元的wi-fi實現和電腦可視的機器人 , 這大約是過去這類型機器人所花費的百分之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他在生物模式中
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他其實是用儀器上的攝影機來跟著我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我往下看 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很溫暖 , 所以他會把眼光留在我身上 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來到這裡 , 他會轉過來跟我
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來這裡--他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會像其他生物一樣感到害怕 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以 , 在很多方面 , romo就像一隻有自己想法的寵物 。

so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他實際上在任何兩個智慧裝置之間串流雙向音頻和影片 。
