so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	所以我們之前談到遠距離 , 這是個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	你可以想像一個八歲的女孩 , 例如 , 誰有iphone , 她媽媽會買她一個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 寄電子郵件給祖母 , 她住在國家的另一邊 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	奶奶可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩躲藏 , 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則她只能看到她孫女一、兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	所以這些是romo今天能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想談談我們未來正在努力的事物 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這其實是我們其中一個工程師 , 多姆 , 在一個週末建造的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	建立在一個叫blockly的google公開框架上 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這可以讓你拖著、丟下這些半音代碼的積木 , 為你想要的機器人創造任何行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何為romo創造一個行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你可以在瀏覽器中模擬這種行為 , 就是你在左邊看到romo在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它下載到你的機器人上 , 在現實生活中執行它 , 執行現實生活中的程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有你感到驕傲的東西 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些wi-fi的機器人都彼此學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以這麼專注於建立機器人 , 讓每個人都能訓練 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人領域中 , 最引人入勝的使用案件是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	他們從人轉變為人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以我們認為 , 如果你要在家裡有機器人 , 那機器人應該要成為你自己的想像力的一種表現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來會是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我完全不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道的是 , 它不是10年或100億美金 , 或一個大型的人形機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它將取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 例如romo , 以及像你們一樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們等不及要讓你們全部的機器人 , 我們等不及要看你建造什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和行動主義者伊莎貝爾•阿言德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義當然 , 在這場演講中 , 還有熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女人、世界文化、
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德訴說熱情的故事 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你 。 在這裡真的很可怕 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我在這裡告訴各位一些熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有個猶太人說我很喜歡 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼是真理 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是個說故事的人 。 我想傳達一些比我們共同人性更真實的東西 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都感興趣 , 有些縈繞在我 , 直到最後寫出來為止 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	某些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們身邊的謎團 , 所以我寫下巧合、預期、情緒、夢想、大自然的力量、魔力 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我發表了幾本書 , 但我一直住在匿名狀態 , 直到2006年2月 , 當時我帶著奧運國際奧運的奧運國旗 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	那讓我成為了名人 。 現在人們在macy's中認出我 , 而我的孫子認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	允許我告訴你們我四分鐘的名氣 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧林匹克典禮的組織者之一 , 開幕典禮的其中一位 , 打電話給我 , 說我被選為一個旗幟選手 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回覆說 , 這是個錯誤認同的案例 , 因為我離身為運動員的最遠之處 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	其實 , 我甚至不確定我可以到體育場去沒有助行器 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是笑的物質 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次只有婦女會帶著奧運國旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性代表五大洲 , 還有三位奧運金牌贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	一個制服 , 她說 , 並尋求我的衡量 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我在一個流暢的反感中看到了我自己 , 看起來像一個米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中期 , 我發現自己在土耳其 , 熱情的群眾在80個奧運小組中歡呼 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了一切在遊戲中競爭 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得贏 , 但有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一股雪 , 一英吋的冰 , 風力 , 可以決定一個賽跑或比賽的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的是訓練或運氣是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且有決心的心才能拿到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	一切都是熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	土耳其的街道被紅海報報報導宣佈奧運的口號
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情存在這裡 。 不是總是如此 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們 , 並決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這是我書中的角色需要的:熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要mavericks , 異議者 , 冒險家 , 外人和叛軍 , 他們會問問題 , 彎曲規則 , 並冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有常識的人並不會做有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會做出好的前配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育館的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了其他國旗熊:三位運動員 , 女演員蘇珊•沙倫和索菲亞•羅倫 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	還有 , 兩個有熱情心的女性:旺加里馬達尼 , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 她種植了三千萬棵樹 。 透過這麼做 , 她改變了土壤、天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然 , 在許多村落中的一些地方 , 還有經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	蘇曼是柬埔寨的激進分子 , 熱切地對抗兒童賣淫 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	她14歲時 , 她祖父把她賣給妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 被男人強暴的小女孩 , 她相信 , 和一個很年輕的處女做愛 , 會從愛滋病中治癒她們 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	而在兒童被迫接收五、十五名客戶的妓院中 , 如果他們反抗 , 他們就會用電擊來折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色房間裡我收到我的制服
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的那種外衣 , 但它離我預期的米其林套裝還很遠 。 不是很糟 , 真的 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但 , 大部分的旗幟 , 除了蘇菲雅羅倫 , 普遍代表美與熱情的象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過70歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感 , 很低 , 又很高 , 帶著很深的坦白 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	現在 , 你怎麼能有一個很深的坦克車 , 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當在電視訪問中問: 「 她怎麼可能看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 。 我的背總是直立的 , 我沒有讓老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 這裡有來自地球上最漂亮的女性之一的自由建議 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有噁心 , 沒有咳嗽 , 沒有呼吸 , 沒有跟自己說話 , 沒有遙控 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有這麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜的某個時點 , 我們被召喚到體育館的翅膀 , 大聲疾呼的人宣佈奧林匹克旗 , 音樂一開始是順帶一提 , 也是從這裡開始的音樂 , aida遊行的音樂 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	索菲亞.羅倫就在我面前 , 她比我高一英尺 , 不算頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走路 , 像非洲大草原上的長頸鹿 , 肩膀上拿著旗子 。 我在背後開著腳趾抱著旗 , 伸出手臂 , 這樣我的頭就在該死的旗子下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的攝影機都在索菲亞 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分的媒體照片中我也出現 , 雖然在蘇菲雅的腿間經常出現 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大部分男人都很想當的地方
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘是奧運體育館裡的那些 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	當我說這句話時 , 我的丈夫會被冒犯 , 雖然我已經向他解釋 , 我們在私人的做法通常只需要不到四分鐘 , 所以他不該親自接受 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有那四個壯觀的時刻所有的按鈕 , 因為我不想忘記在老年時摧毀我的腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠帶著奧運熱情的關鍵字
so here's a tale of passion .	以下是熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	年份是1998年 , 地方是剛果utsi難民的監獄 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順帶一提 , 世界上有80%的難民和流離失所的人是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以把這個地方稱為剛果一個死囚營 , 因為那些沒有被殺的人會死於疾病或餓死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 蘿絲•卡倫多 , 還有她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕和寡婦
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵們強迫她看著她的丈夫被折磨和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的她能夠讓她七個孩子活著 , 幾個月後 , 她生了個產前雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子剪斷臍帶 , 用自己的頭髮連接起來 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她以雙胞胎為名 , 在營地的指揮官取得他們的利益之後 , 用黑茶餵食他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持他們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵在她的牢房裡闖來強暴她最老的女兒時 , 她會抓著她 , 拒絕放手 , 即使他們拿著一把槍抵著她的頭 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家庭存活了十六個月 , 接著 , 透過非凡的運氣 , 以及一位年輕的美國男子的熱情心 , 薩莎•查諾夫 , 他想辦法把她放進美國救援飛機 , 羅斯•地圖 , 和她的九個孩子最後到達亞利桑那州鳳凰城 , 在那裡生活和茁壯茁壯 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	在斯瓦希里語中 , 繪製出偉大的愛情 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我的書的主角是強而有熱情的女性 , 像蘿絲•卡倫多 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我沒有把它們造出來 , 沒有任何需要 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處看到他們 ,
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一輩子都和女性一起工作 。
i know them well .	我很清楚他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古代 , 在世界末日 , 在父權天主教和保守的家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪五歲時我是個激進的女性主義者雖然尚未接觸到智利 , 所以沒人知道我到底出了什麼問題 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 有很高的代價可以支付我的自由 , 且要質疑父權制度 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付錢 , 因為為了我收到的每一塊炸彈 , 我得以遞出兩顆 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我的女兒保拉在她二十幾歲時 , 她對我說女權主義是約會的 , 我應該繼續走下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有一場難忘的戰鬥 。 女權主義是約會的 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	沒錯 , 對於我女兒和今天在場的所有人 , 但對世界上其他大部分的姊妹來說 , 仍然被強迫結婚 , 賣淫 , 強迫他們有孩子不想要 , 或無法餵飽 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法控制自己的身體或生活 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育和沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、被毆打 , 有時會被處罰 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對現今大部分西方的年輕女性來說 , 被稱為女性主義者是一種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女性主義從來沒有性感 , 但讓我向各位保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我調情過 , 我從來沒有缺乏男性 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義沒有死 , 沒有任何意義 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞 , 改變它 , 對女神來說 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱它為金星、金星、或是bimbo , 或任何你想要的東西 ; 名字不重要 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這是另一個充滿熱情的故事這是一個悲傷的故事
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	地方是孟加拉的一個小女子診所 。
the year is 2005 .	年份是2005年
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫 , 在她的三週度度假期間 , 他去診所當志工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備乾淨牙齒 , 但當她到那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一間滿蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一行婦女等了好幾個小時被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人處於極端疼痛之中 , 因為她有好幾隻腐爛的臼齒 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮意識到唯一的解決方案是拉出不好的牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她不是為此授權的 , 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她冒著很大的風險 , 且她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有合適的樂器 , 但很幸運的是 , 她帶來了一些novocaine 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有勇敢和熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她向一間禱告 , 帶著手術前進 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 鬆了一口氣的病人親吻她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生人員再抽出許多牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 當她再來到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人正在和她丈夫一起等待她 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女人的臉看起來像水梅隆 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	腫大到你根本看不見眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫 , 憤怒 , 威脅要殺死美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做過的事感到害怕 , 但後來翻譯解釋 , 病人的狀況和操作沒有任何關係 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她的丈夫打她 , 因為她不在家裡準備晚餐給他 。
millions of women live like this today .	今天有數百萬名像這樣的女性生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人中最窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然女性有三分之二的勞工 , 卻擁有不到世界資產的百分之一 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	她們的薪水比男性低於男性 , 如果她們有薪水 , 她們會保持脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 她們會不斷受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實是 , 給予女性教育、工作、控制自己的收入、繼承和財產的能力 , 讓社會受惠 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予權力 , 她的孩子和她的家庭會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落的繁榮 , 最終 , 整個國家也是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai到肯亞的一個村莊
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和婦女談話 , 並解釋土地是貧瘠的 , 因為他們已經砍伐和賣掉樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女種植新的樹木 , 並澆水 , 再下降 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五六年之內 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤豐富 , 村莊就被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最後退的社會總是那些放下女性的人 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而這個顯而易見的事實卻被政府忽略 , 也被慈善事業所忽略 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	每一美元給一個婦女計劃 , 20美元被給予男性計劃 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦予他們力量 , 將會改變一切 , 勝過科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性合作連結、受教育 , 能將和平和繁榮帶到這個漏洞的星球 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡都是平民百姓 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 他們是重度傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人經營世界 , 看看我們所遇到的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大多數人在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序是合理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個保存生命的世界 , 生活品質豐富了每個人 , 不僅是為了特權而豐富的世界 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	在一月 , 我看到了費南多•波特羅在加州大學柏克萊圖書館的畫展 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國沒有博物館或藝廊 , 除了帶著波特羅的作品的紐約畫廊以外 , 也不敢展示這幅畫因為主題是阿布格拉伊布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是折磨和濫用權力的巨大畫作 , 在彈性botero風格中 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我沒有辦法從腦中或心中得到那些影像 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是用 「 不當 」 的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用的權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們的物種中 , 雄性領袖定義現實 , 並迫使其餘的群體接受現實並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則會隨時改變 , 但它們總是會受益 , 在這個例子中 , 棘手的效果 , 在經濟學上並沒有效果 , 完美地工作 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待的把戲從階梯頂端移到底部 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	婦女和兒童 , 尤其是窮人 , 在最底層
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	連男人中最多的人都有他們可以虐待女人或小孩的人 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	透過性別、收入、種族 , 和階級 , 我得到的力量 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時間是崛起的 , 要在我們的文明中做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但 , 為了真正的改變 , 我們需要全世界的女性化能源 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要在權力的位置上有關鍵數量的女性 , 我們需要培養男性內在的女性能源 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我指的是有年輕心靈的男人 , 當然
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老傢伙毫無希望 ; 我們得等他們死 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很想擁有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 若有選擇 , 我寧願有威加里馬塔伊的戰士心 , 主要是哺乳、珍妮 , 以及玫瑰地圖 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得更好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是要讓它更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不呢 ? 這是有可能的 。 看看這個房間裡所有這些知識、能源、才華和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	咱們放下我們的花俏 , 捲起袖子 , 開始工作 , 熱切地 , 創造出幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦大小的城市中 , 有三千萬份餐會被服務 。 但所有的食物都來自何方 ? 建築師卡洛琳鋼鐵討論每天餵養一個城市的奇蹟 , 並展現出古老食物路線如何塑造了現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡洛琳.斯特爾:食物如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	如何餵飽一座城市
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代的偉大問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問到
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們視為理所當然 , 如果我們進到商店或餐廳 , 或到這個劇院的一小時內 , 將會有食物在那等著我們 , 神奇地從某處來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為 , 對於倫敦大小的城市來說 , 每一天 , 足夠的食物必須被生產、運輸、買、買、賣、被煮熟、被吃掉、被丟棄的城市 , 類似的事情每天都要發生 , 對於地球上的每個城市而言 , 這是很了不起的 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這樣的地方 , 彷彿他們是世界上最自然的東西 , 忘了它 , 因為我們是動物 , 而我們是需要吃的 , 我們其實和我們古老的祖先一樣依賴自然世界 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們進入城市 , 越是自然世界被轉化成非凡的地景 , 像我身後的黃豆田 , 在巴西的馬托格羅索 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的地景 , 但很少人能看到它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	而漸漸地這些景觀 , 不只是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們更多搬進城市 , 更多人吃肉 , 全球每年三分之一的穀物現在被餵給動物 , 而不是給我們人類的動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於它需要三倍的穀物 , 只需要十倍的穀物來餵飽人類 , 如果它先經過一隻動物 , 那不是非常有效率的餵食方式 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是個不斷增加的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到了2050年 , 估計有兩倍的人會住在城市裡 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	同時也估計將有兩倍的肉和乳類消耗 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以肉類和都市主義在手上興起 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將帶來一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 飢餓的食用量達到60億 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 如果我們隨身攜帶 , 這是個我們無法解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有9百萬公頃的雨林已經失去 , 創造出新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	儘管同時我們也失去了相當多現有的耕地來鹽化和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也很渴望石化燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	大約需要十卡路里來生產我們在西方所消耗的每一卡路里 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	即使我們有大量成本生產的食物 , 我們其實並不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國生產的食物有一半是目前丟棄的 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	為了結束這一切 , 在這漫長的過程中 , 我們甚至沒有妥善管理來餵飽地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	十億人是肥胖的 , 此外還有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	完全沒有道理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為 , 目前糧食中有80%的全球貿易只由五個跨國企業所掌控 , 這是一張嚴峻的照片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們進入城市 , 世界也擁抱西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 這是不可持續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要解答稍微簡單的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 這個過程的開端 , 是在東邊的古代 , 也就是所謂的肥沃 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是最近形狀的 。
and it was also fertile .	同時也是肥沃的
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約一萬年前 , 這裡有兩項非凡的發明 , 農業和城市主義 , 大約發生在同一地點 , 同時發生 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這並不是偶然的 , 因為農業和城市是有限的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們古老祖先第一次發現的穀物 , 產生了足夠大且穩定的食物來源 , 來支撐永久的居住地 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看那些居住地是什麼樣子 , 我們會發現它們很完整 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被生產力的農場土地包圍 , 被大型的寺廟複合體支配 , 像是烏爾的這一區 , 實際上 , 是精神化的 , 中央糧食分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為那是寺廟 , 整理收穫 , 聚集在穀物中 , 提供給眾神 , 然後提供給眾神所不吃的穀物 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你願意 , 這些城市的靈性和實體生活都被穀物和收穫所支配 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	而事實上 , 每座古老城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是所有人都這麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	著名的是 , 羅馬在第一世紀時約有一百萬公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市本身是如何飼養的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是我所謂的 「 古老食物里 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬能取得海水 , 讓它可以從很長的路途中運送食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是唯一能夠在古代這樣做的方式 , 因為要在路上運送食物是非常困難的 , 這很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物很快就消失了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以 , 羅馬有效率地對卡車和埃及這些地方進行戰爭 , 只為了在穀物保護區上取得它的爪子 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張真的是非常長的 , 吸引了軍事化的購物速度 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到這個:羅馬是以前從倫敦出口的牡蠣 , 在一個階段 。 我想那是非凡的 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬透過胃口塑造了它的印度陸地 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事也發生在工業前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀倫敦的地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 它的穀物是從泰姆斯身上進來的 , 沿著這張地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場到城市的南方
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	這些道路從它們變成便宜的 , 主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街的名字 , 你可以分辨出300年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	魚類也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也被河流侵襲 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 比爾大門是倫敦的魚市場 , 一直到1980年代中期 , 才開始營運 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這真的很不尋常 , 當你想到
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他人都在遊走 , 裝著像磚塊般的手機 , 有點像港口上的魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是城市中食物的另一個特點:一旦它的根源被建立起來 , 它們就很少移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉是個非常不同的故事 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進城市裡 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦的大量肉品來自西北部 , 來自蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它就進來了 , 抵達西北部的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦非常著名的肉市場 , 位在上面 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	藝術家從東安格利亞來到東北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像天氣女人這樣做 。 總之 , 鳥兒們都帶著腳進來 , 用小的畫布鞋來保護牠們 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當他們抵達便宜的東部時 , 他們就被賣掉了 , 這就是為什麼被稱為 「 農業 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看工業時代任何城市的地圖 , 你可以追溯到食物的來源 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物所塑造的 , 兩者都透過閱讀街道的名字 , 這給你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	週五的街道 , 在以前的生活中 , 是你在星期五去買你的魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也必須想像它滿是食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一購買食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密斯菲爾德的畫面 , 你可以看到 , 在這樣的城市生活會非常困難 , 且不知道你的食物從哪裡來 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你在星期日午餐時 , 有機會在你的窗外滑翔 , 大約三天前 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機的城市 , 一個有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	然後十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年偉大西方的圖像 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 一些最早的火車乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以 , 突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被從視力和心靈的某處被屠殺 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	並藉由鐵路進入城市 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 首次在任何地方種植城市 , 真正的大小和形狀 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	以前城市受到地理限制 ; 以前 , 他們必須透過非常困難的身體手段來取得他們的食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們從地理上有效地解放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	從這些倫敦的地圖可以看到 , 在火車經過90年後 , 火車來臨後 , 火車經過了一小塊 , 很容易被動物送進來 , 如此一來 , 到一個很大的星球 , 非常非常難餵飽任何人 , 不論是動物或人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然這只是開端 。 火車來了車之後 , 這真的是這過程的結尾 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是城市的最後解放 , 來自於任何明顯和自然的關係 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	而這就是那種逃避氣味、逃避混亂的城市 , 當然也沒有人會想在這樣的景觀中走路 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們為了取得食物而做的是 , 他們在車子裡 , 開車到外圍某處的一個箱子 , 回來後面帶著一個禮拜的購物回來 , 想知道 , 地球上要怎麼處理它 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這是我們與食物和城市之間的關係的時刻 , 完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有以前是市中心的食物 , 周圍的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	曾經是社交活動 , 買賣和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會煮飯 , 現在只要加水 , 或加點蛋 , 如果你在做蛋糕或其他的東西 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只是在一個包裝上讀到背後的標籤
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	而且我們不重視食物 , 也不信任
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是去評價它 , 我們把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統的偉大諷刺之一 , 就是他們已經做出了他們承諾要更加容易的事 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由在任何地方建立城市和任何地方 , 它們其實已經讓我們與最重要的關係有了距離 , 那就是我們和大自然的關係 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	而且他們也讓我們依賴的系統 , 只有它們能夠傳遞出去 , 如我們所見 , 才是不可持續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們該怎麼做呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前 , 湯瑪斯更自問的是
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》的最前期 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	那是一系列的半獨立城市 , 如果這聽起來很熟悉 , 一天的走路 , 每個人基本上都是農業的走路 , 在他們的後花園裡種植蔬菜 , 吃起來的餐點 , 等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你可以主張 , 食物是烏托邦的基本秩序原則 , 即使從來沒有這樣框架過 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	還有另一個非常著名的 「 烏托邦 」 視野 , 埃貝內茲霍華 , 「 花園城市 」 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列的半獨立城市 , 一小片大都市 , 一塊可耕地 , 加入了另一塊鐵路 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	同樣的 , 食物可以被說是他視力的秩序原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來 , 但和默斯克韋茲的願景沒有任何關係 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是烏托邦的想法的問題 , 他們是烏托邦人 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯•摩爾刻意使用的字 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	那是個笑話 , 因為它有來自希臘語的雙向衍生 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可能意味著一個好地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的 , 一個想像的東西 , 我們不能擁有
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念性的工具 , 來思考人類居住的深層問題 , 這讓它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 就是西托邦 , 來自古希臘 , 「 西托斯 」 為食物 , 和 「 湯波斯 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西托邦
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們可以利用食物作為一個非常強大的工具--一個概念的工具 , 設計工具 , 以不同的方式形塑這個世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這樣做 , simtopia會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	嗯 , 我想這看起來有點像
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 , 只是狗的臉上的表情
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	但無論如何 , 這是生活的中心食物 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌 , 被享受 , 人們花時間為此 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這是我們社會中應該有食物的地方 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你不可能有這樣的場景 , 除非你有這樣的人 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順帶一提 , 這些人也可以是男人 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	是那些想到食物的人 , 認為前面的人 , 計畫的人 , 可以盯著一堆原本蔬菜 , 實際認可他們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 。 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這類人 , 我們就不可能有這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我故意選擇這個 , 因為這是一個男人買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網絡、食物在當地生長的市場
it's common . it's fresh .	很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	成為城市社會生活的一部分
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為若沒有這些 , 你就不能有這種地方 , 當地種植的食物 , 同時也成為地景的一部分 , 而不僅是零用商品 , 在某些不可見的地獄之中 。
cows with a view .	牛的觀點
steaming piles of humus .	蒸汽堆的humus
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	基本上就是把整件事情整合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一間溫室 , 在那裡 , 孩子們可以告訴所有有關食物和種植自己的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一種叫凱文的植物 , 或它是屬於一個叫做凱文的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但無論如何 , 這類企圖將我們與大自然重新連結的項目是極其重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 西托邦 , 對我來說 , 真的是一種看法 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上是意識到西托邦已經存在於各處的小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅是加入他們 , 把食物當作一種看法 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們就會停止把城市視為大型、大都會化、不生產力的斑點 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們將看到它們更像這樣 , 作為生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 它們是無可避免的一部分 , 相互連結的 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	當然 , 這也不是很棒的圖像 , 因為我們不需要再像這樣生產食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要考慮更多關於永續發展 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖片能總結出我們需要做的那種想法 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	對於食物塑造我們生活的方式的重新概念化
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道最好的影像是從650年前
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	是阿布羅基歐.羅倫澤蒂的《好政府的寓言》 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	關於城市和鄉村之間的關係
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我想這方面的訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧國家 , 國家會照顧城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在想問 , 如果他今天畫出這張圖片 , 阿布洛吉歐.羅倫澤蒂會畫什麼呢 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天好的政府會長什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須問的 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃的東西
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們必須意識到 , 世界也是我們所吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採用這個想法 , 我們可以用食物作為一個很強大的工具 , 來更好地形塑這個世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	數週從慈悲憲章發起 , 卡倫•阿姆斯壯在21世紀中探討宗教的角色:它的教條會把我們分開嗎 ? 還是它會讓我們團結成共通的善人嗎 ? 她審視催化劑 , 能驅動世界的信仰 , 來重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , ted大獎 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 宗教 , tedglobal2009 , 暴力事件 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重現黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我一直感到沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我開始敏銳地意識到 , 在所有主要世界的信仰中 , 同情心的核心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個都演化出了他們自己的版本所謂的黃金法則
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 它會出現在正面的版本 「 總是把其他人當作你想要對待自己 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本 「 不要對別人做你不會喜歡的 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心 , 發現是什麼讓你感到痛苦 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情境下 , 在任何其他人身上 , 去發炎那痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	而人們強調同情的重要性 , 不只是因為這聽起來不錯 , 而是因為它有用 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了黃金法則 , 如同司法所說: 「 一整天 , 每一天 , 不僅是做好事的一個問題 , 然後回到貪婪和自我主義的一生中 , 而是一整天都在做 , 你將自己從世界的中心 , 放到另一邊 , 你超越了自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它帶你進入了所謂的上帝、涅盤、拉馬、泰奧的存在 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知的自我存在的東西 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道很多時候這對宗教生活是如此的核心
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些奇妙的例外 , 當宗教人士聚在一起時 , 宗教領袖們聚在一起 , 他們爭論的是關於異教徒的論點 , 或是說出一個仇恨的議會 , 或對同性戀的激勵 , 或類似的東西 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們不太想有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我在和宗教人士談話時 , 有點像是在表情中 , 穿越他們的臉孔 , 因為人們常常想要是對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	那當然會打敗運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我對ted這麼感激 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們很溫柔地從我的書線性研究帶我進入21世紀 , 讓我能和一個比我想像中更廣泛的觀眾交談 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到很急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們沒有辦法在全球實施黃金法則 , 這樣我們對待所有人 , 無論他們在哪裡或誰 , 彷彿他們和我們一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 來交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代的一個偉大的任務 , 就是建立一個全球性的社會 , 如我所說 , 人們可以在和平中住在一起 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該做出重大貢獻的宗教反而被視為問題的一部分
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 這不僅僅是相信黃金法則的宗教人士
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這種有同理心的想像行為 , 把自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有一個選擇 , 對我來說 ,
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續帶出去 , 或是強調我們信仰的教條和寬容面 , 或我們可以回到拉比之下 。 拉比希爾 , 耶穌的老一代 , 拉比希爾 , 他被一位猶太人請來總結整個猶太教條 , 他站在一條腿上 , 說: 「 這對你來說很討厭 , 不要跟你的鄰居說 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那就是托拉和其他一切都只是評論而已 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	而教會的拉比和早期的父親說 , 任何能詮釋仇恨和不尊重的劇本都是不合法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	而我們需要重振那精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不只是因為愛的精神把我們拋下去 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這一切成真 , 用ted所介紹的現代溝通來達成 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對我們所有伴侶的反應感到極大的開心 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一個團體要用憲章來治癒分裂 , 最近已經在新加坡社會中蔓延 , 還有國會的一些成員想要在政治上實施它 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一個藝術展覽 , 讓藝術家能夠帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 並向他們展示 , 慈悲同時也躺在所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社群在舉辦活動和討論 , 都在討論伊斯蘭和所有信仰的核心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停在那裡 , 不能用發射器停止 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教義 , 這是我們犯錯的地方 , 完全集中在相信異教的教義 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教學一定會導致行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	直到我死去的那一天 , 我還是打算要工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我還想繼續和我們的夥伴一起做兩件事教育和刺激同情心的思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育因為我們太脫離同情心了
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常認為這意味著對某人感到遺憾 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但當然你不了解同情心如果你只想一想 ,
you also have to do it .	你也必須去做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能參與媒體 , 因為媒體是很重要的 , 幫助我們解析一些我們對其他人的刻板印象 , 這讓我們從彼此的角度分裂 。
the same applies to educators .	同樣的應用在教育家身上
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望青年能感受到一種動態 , 一種充滿同情的生活方式的動態和挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到 , 它要求急性智能 , 不只是一種美好的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想打電話給學者 , 來探索他們自己的同情心主題 , 以及其他人的傳統 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	最重要的是 , 鼓勵對於不寬容說話的敏感度 , 如此一來 , 由於人們有這份憲章 , 不論他們的信仰或缺乏這些信念 , 他們覺得有能力去挑戰不寬容的言論 , 來自他們的宗教領袖、他們的政治領袖 , 來自產業界的首領 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過要把憲章放在網路上 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我還被困在舊的世界裡 , 一大群boffins坐在一間房間裡 , 還在追求另一位arcane的陳述 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted向我介紹了一種全新的思考方式和呈現想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這就是ted的精彩之處 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有這些專長 , 如果我們加入全部一起 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 問題有時似乎是不可思議的 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但我想引用最後的一句話 , 說到英國作者的一句話 , 一位牛津作者 , 我不常引用過的 , c.s.s.路易斯的話 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一件事 , 自從我在學校讀書時 , 困在我心裡 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的書《四個愛》中
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他把愛情區別開 , 當兩個人凝視著 , 咒語 , 凝視著對方的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把這和友誼比較 , 當兩個人站在一旁時 , 肩並肩 , 雙眼固定在共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 但我們也可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	而我深信
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我強烈感受到 , 在我們在vevey的小小蓄意中 , 當所有不同說服的人聚在一起時 , 一邊為共同的目標努力 , 一邊工作 , 一邊為共同的目標 , 差異會融化 。
and we learn amity .	而我們學到的是野心 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學會了一起生活 , 去認識彼此 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝大家 。
david macaulay relives the winding and sometimes surreal journey toward the completion of rome antics , his illustrated homage to the historic city .	davidmacaulay將風力復甦 , 有時是超現實的旅程 , 朝著羅馬反思的補充 , 他向歷史城市致敬 。
macarthur grant , art , arts , book , cities , communication , culture , design , entertainment , humor , storytelling	macarthurgrant、藝術、書籍、城市、溝通、文化、設計、娛樂、幽默、說故事 。
i draw to better understand things .	我為了更好的理解而畫畫 。
sometimes i make a lot of drawings and i still don't understand what it is i'm drawing .	有時我會畫很多畫 , 我仍然不了解我在畫什麼 。
those of you who are comfortable with digital stuff and even smug about that relationship might be amused to know that the guy who is best known for " the way things work , " while preparing for part of a panel for called understanding , spent two days trying to get his laptop to communicate with his new cd burner .	那些對數位化的東西感到自在的人 , 甚至會對那關係感到自在 , 會很高興知道 , 那個最為人所知的傢伙 , 為 「 事物運作 」 做準備 , 同時準備一個名為 「 理解 」 的部分 , 花了兩天的時間 , 試圖讓他的筆記型電腦和他的新cdburner溝通 。

i've always managed my own extensions so it never even occurred to me to read the instructions , but i did finally figure it out . i had to figure it out , because along with the invitation came the frightening reminder that there would be no projector , so bringing those carousels would no longer be necessary but some alternate form of communication would .	我一直在管理自己的延伸 , 以至於我從來沒有想過要閱讀這些指令 , 但我終於搞懂了 。 我必須搞清楚 。 因為 , 經過邀請 , 提醒了 , 沒有投影機 , 所以 , 把那些旋轉器再也沒有必要了 , 但有些替代的交流形式 。
now , i could talk about something that i'm known for , something that would be particularly appropriate for many of the more technically minded people here , or i could talk about something i really care about .	現在 , 我可以談談我所熟知的事物 , 一些特別適合在技術上的人 , 或是我可以談論我真正關心的事物 。
i decided to go with the latter .	我決定和後者一起去 。

now , why would i care about rome , particularly ?	那我為什麼要特別關心羅馬呢 ?
well , i went to rhode island school of design in the second half of the '60s to study architecture .	嗯 , 我去了羅德島設計學院 , 在60年代的後半 , 去研究建築 。
i was lucky enough to spend my last year , my fifth year , in rome as a student . it changed my life .	我很幸運 , 去年 , 我的第五年 , 在羅馬擔任學生 。 這改變了我的一生 。
not the least reason was the fact that i had spent those first four years living at home , driving into risd everyday , driving back .	並非最不理由是我在家裡度過那四年的事實 , 每天開車進rsid , 開車回來 。
i missed the '60s . i read about them ; i understand they were pretty interesting . i missed them , but i did spend that extraordinary year in rome , and it's a place that is never far from my mind .	我錯過了60年代 , 我讀到有關他們的事 ; 我明白他們很有趣 。 我錯過了他們 , 但我確實在羅馬度過了那不平凡的一年 , 那是一個離我心中不遠的地方 。
so , whenever given an opportunity , i try to do something in it or with it or for it .	所以 , 只要有機會 , 我會試著用它來做點什麼 , 或用它 。

these are just drawings of rome . i get back as often as possible i need to .	這些只是羅馬的繪圖 , 我盡可能多回頭 。
all different materials , all different styles , all different times , drawings from sketchbooks looking at the details of rome .	各種不同的材料 , 各種不同的風格 , 各種不同的時期 , 從草圖書中畫出來的 , 看著羅馬的細節 。
part of the reason i'm showing you these is that it sort of helps illustrate this process i go through of trying to figure out what it is i feel about rome and why i feel it .	我給你們看的部分原因是 , 它能協助說明這個過程 , 我試圖找出我對羅馬的感受 , 以及為什麼我會感受到它 。

if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺疊頁 , 讓你直接展開它 , 你看它背後的我所謂的疤痕組織 。

you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把你頭上的頁面包起來 , 在那短暫的時間內 。

ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不打開這本書 , 如果我把它打開90度 , 我們就向下看著萬神廟的前面 , 我們看起來有點像頂部 , 或多或少在廣場上 。

no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺痕 , 沒有把戲 , 只是一本沒有打開的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這看起來很有前景 。 我想 , 也許我會在裡面做 , 我甚至可以把摺痕和唯一一部分開放的書結合在一起 。

so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 如果你試著讓人們注意一本書 , 一路上拿起資訊 , 這總是件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進展 」 把我當作抓到的標題 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果是一隻鴿子 , 它會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德賽 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是那趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我是說 , 如果一個標題是可行的 , 使用它 。 但這會是一段穿越羅馬的旅程 , 展示所有我喜歡羅馬的事情 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	一隻鴿子坐在教堂上方
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天起飛 , 做正常鴿子的東西 。 回來 , 整個地方都被支架和綠色網子包覆著 , 這種鴿子沒辦法回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以現在是一隻無家可歸的鴿子 , 牠要找另一個住處 , 這讓我可以穿過我最喜歡的東西的目錄 , 我們從最高的鴿子開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許牠必須回去和家人住在一起 ; 這並非總是件好事 , 但牠又會再次把鴿子聚在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有一個人應該以某種方式參與其中 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老傢伙 , 他花了一輩子照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到哪裡去找他們危險的地方 , 他們會變成和這個傢伙的朋友 , 學會為他做個招式 , 用午餐時間娛樂他 , 諸如此類 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	有一個真正的債券在這個老人和這些鴿子之間發展 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事結束時真的生病了 。

and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於得到足夠的力量 , 把梯子爬到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , 一個拉紅色的氣球 , 在那裡等著他 , 然後他們把他帶到市中心的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這一點:每當他失去一隻鴿子時 , 他就會把那隻鴿子帶到城市外的牆上 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在舊的羅馬習俗中 , 死者從來沒有被埋在牆內 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這真的是個非常歡呼的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	真的要走很長一段路 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷了......再一次 , 如果包裝沒有效果 , 如果故事沒有到哪裡去 , 我只是想出了頭銜 , 希望一個標題能把我從正確的方向踢下去 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時 , 它的確足夠專注我 , 我甚至會做個頭銜 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	這些都是標題頁面 , 最終引領我去解答我定下的方案 , 這是一位年輕女子的故事 , 她在寄宿鴿子上傳訊息 , 她住在羅馬市外的牆壁上 , 到城裡的某人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	而鴿子正往上飛 , 往上飛 ,
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	一路上你可以看到墓碑和松子等等 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你看到鴿子的軌跡 ; 如果你看不到紅線 , 你就是那隻鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	在這個時點 , 它變得有必要且可能 , 試著傳達那種感覺在城市中飛行 , 而不動 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	過去cestius的金字塔看起來很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常的東西 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件大部份住鴿子都不做的事:它採用了這條景象路線 , 這是我覺得要把這本書延伸到大約四頁以外的地方 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	我們圍繞著競技場 , 穿越了聖母院的聖母教堂 , 以及海克力士朝向河流的神廟 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎碰撞到米開朗基羅所設計的palazzofarnes所設計的好處米開朗基羅建造的石頭從柱狀的狹窄逃出去
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯瞰柬埔寨德菲奧里
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給學生看的其中一件事 , 因為這是一個完全的基礎化--一種否認任何觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一的觀點法則是 , 如果它看起來是可信的 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出消失點在哪裡 , 火星和其他幾個在克雷蒙亞 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但 , 在聖母瑪莉亞德拉斯前面的皮亞扎 , 在那裏 , 一個足球比賽正在進行中 , 我們被一個足球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	現在這張圖表很糟糕 , 被足球撞擊 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的作品:有聖母瑪莉亞德拉斯的步調 , 有足球 , 有一點鳥的翅膀沒有發生 , 所以我必須重新思考一下 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想看到聖母瑪莉亞德拉斯的步調 , 這些書真的很靈活 , 非常有互動性 , 只是轉過來 , 用另一種方式看 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過巷子 , 我們可以看到影響力在紅線中被捕捉 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	然後鳥類會把自己拉到這個中世紀的高塔裡 , 少數幾個中世紀的高塔之一 , 移向聖母堂的教堂 , 在圓頂上 , 往下看 , 向下看我們已經提過的比薩納伏納 , 看了幾次 , 看到和流動 ; 這裡有著伯尼尼亞的雕像 , 穿越了四條河 , 接著 , 穿越了美妙的布羅米尼亞米特的聖誕節 , 停在26英尺的直徑上 , 停止了足夠長的時間 , 來抓住我們的呼吸氣 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們就可以在裡面到處飛 , 因為我們在飛行 , 我們不需要在這個特定時刻擔心地心引力 , 所以這幅畫可以隨時在頁面上指導方向 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們會有點興奮 , 不意外地模仿建築 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	在我剛才談到的那個美麗的牆上 , 充滿了我所談的焦點 ; 漂亮的雕刻設置在新月球上方的牆壁上 , 「 崛起者 」 的標誌 , 等等 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後 , 我們抵達了帕拉索州的庭院 , 也就是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 到一個小窗口進入閣樓 , 在那裡有人在畫板工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他把訊息從鳥的腿上除去 ; 這是它所說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著繪圖板 , 我們看到他正在做的是 , 事實上 , 一隻鴿子剛剛拍攝的旅程地圖 , 紅線會透過所有的視線延伸 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要資訊 , 這樣我們就完成了這個 「 理解 」 的循環 , 你只需要閱讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的研究人員自行組合這個想法 , 與其建造某樣東西 , 我們能創造出一些材料 , 來建造它們自己 , 非常像dnazips本身的方式 。 這是早期階段的一個很大的概念 ; tibbits向我們展示了三顆獨特的項目 , 它暗示了自我組裝的未來可能是什麼樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	skylartibbits:我們能製造出製造自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想向大家展示我們製造東西的方式的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快我們的建築物和機器會自行組合、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以我要給你們看我所相信的 , 是目前製造的狀態 , 然後和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以 , 在目前的製造狀態中 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間組裝 , 有五十萬到一百萬個零件 , 相當複雜、嶄新的、令人興奮的科技 , 在鋼筋、水泥、玻璃中 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空五年的組裝時間 , 250萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你觀察自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬納秒摺疊 , 或是有三十億個鹼基對的dna , 我們可以在大約一小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 在我們的自然系統中 , 所有這些複雜性 , 但它們的效率極高 , 遠遠超過任何我們能建造的 , 遠遠超過任何我們能建造的複雜性 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們在能源方面的效率更高 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	而且他們可以為了長壽而修復自己 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以自然系統有某種超級有趣的東西
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能把這些轉化成我們的建設環境 , 那就有了一些令人興奮的潛力 , 以我們建造東西的方式 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以如果我們想在我們的實體環境中自行組合 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的東西的複雜性 , 如此我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要將它解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	然後我們需要可編程的部件 , 可以把序列拿來折疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能讓它啟動的能量 , 讓我們的部分能夠從這個程式中向上摺疊 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	而我們需要某種類型的錯誤修正措施 , 以保證我們已經成功地建立了我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我要給你們看一些我和我同事在麻省理工學院的項目 , 來實現這個自我組合的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩種是麥克洛波特和decibot
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些項目是大規模可重組的機器人--8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	嵌入了機械電裝置 , 感應器
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你要把你想要摺疊出來的東西 , 變成一連串的角度 , 以負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120 , 像這樣 。 所以 , 一連串的角度 , 或一連串的角度 , 你就會透過弦來發出序列 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位的訊息是負120 , 轉到那邊 , 檢查一下 , 然後把它傳給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些傑出的科學家、工程師、設計師 , 都在這個項目上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我想這真的能帶來光線:這真的可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 很多男人為了製造這個8英尺高的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的可以擴大規模嗎 ? 我們真的可以將機器人技術嵌入每個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 看看被動的大自然 , 或是被動地嘗試進行重新配置的可編程 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它會再進一步 , 它會試著進行實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上嵌入了計算最基本的建材 , 數位邏輯閘 , 直接進入你的部分 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是一個nandgate
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個四面體 , 就是要用你的電腦運算的大門 , 你有兩個輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是使用者的輸入 , 就像你正在建造你的磚塊一樣 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一種是從前一塊磚上被放置的
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後給你一個3d空間的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	所以這意味著 , 使用者可以開始把他們想要的磚塊放進去 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它在之前做的事上計算 , 以及你說你想要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 或向上或向下移動 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , [1、1]輸入等同於0的輸出 , 輸出值會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0、0]輸入是一個輸出1的輸出值 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	所以 , 真正的意思是 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有所有的信息嵌入其中 , 包含了建構出來的東西 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	所以這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個例子中 , 我稱它為自體複製 , 因為你的結構含有確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一個部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都嵌入在告訴你們如何修理它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以有能攀登的東西 , 讀取它 , 然後輸出到一個比一個 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	最後一個我會展示的專案叫做偏見鏈 , 它可能是我們目前最激動的自我組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它需要可重組性和可編程性 , 讓它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一連串元素
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每一個元素都完全一模一樣 , 而且它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每條鏈 , 或每一個元素 , 都想要向右或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上是在編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你在告訴每個單位是否應該向右轉或左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈 , 它就會摺疊成任何你編程的配置 , 在這個案例中 , 一個螺旋 , 或在這個案例中 , 兩個立方體在旁邊 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	基本上你可以編寫任何立體的形狀或維度 , 二維立體到這條鏈完全被動 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴了我們未來什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為這告訴我們有新的可能性可以自我組裝、複製、修復我們的實體結構、建築物、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的可編程能力 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從而有了新的計算可能性
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間運算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚都能實際計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是驚人的平行和分散式運算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這對此是令人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我在這裡展示的這些項目只是對這個未來的一小步 , 如果我們為一個新的自組裝世界實施這些新科技 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 繪製了大陸 , 我們甚至去過海底最深的一點兩次 。 剩下的是什麼 , 去探索 ? 生物學家和探險家nathanwolfe暗示了這個答案:幾乎所有事情 。 我們可以開始 , 他說 , 帶著不可思議的小世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nathanwolfe:剩下什麼要探索的 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我拜訪了威斯康辛州的貝洛特
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡榮耀一位偉大的20世紀探險家roychapmanandrews 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他美國自然歷史博物館 , 安德魯斯帶領了一系列的探勘隊伍到尚未發現的地區 , 例如在戈壁沙漠這裡 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	後來他說 , 印第安納瓊斯角色的基礎
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛特時 , 我給了一群中學學生的公開講座 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡要告訴各位 , 如果在ted這裡有任何比在演講更嚇人的東西 , 它會試著把一群人的注意力放在一個45分鐘的講座上 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	演講結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那時起 , 有一個真的困在我身上 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有位年輕女孩站起來 , 她問: 「 我們應該在哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我想我們之中有許多人認為地球上探索的偉大時代已經結束了 , 對下一代而言 , 他們必須去外太空或最深的海洋 , 才能找到探索的重要事物 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	我們真的沒有什麼意義可以探索地球上留下的生物嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想起我在生物學史上最喜歡的探險家之一
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是個未見過的世界的探險家 , martinusbeijerinck 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	因此beijerinck發掘菸草鑲嵌疾病的起因
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是從菸草植物中吸入的果汁 , 他會透過更小的過濾來過濾它 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到達了一個點 , 他覺得在外面一定有一些東西 , 比當時已知的細菌最小的生命形式還要小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他想出了一個名字 , 為他的神秘經紀人
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為拉丁文為 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭開病毒時beijerinck為我們開啟了全新的世界
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒構成了地球上大多數的基因信息 , 超過所有其他形式的生命組合的基因信息 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 已經有了極大的實用應用 , 和這個世界相關的應用 , 像是天花的根除 , 一種對抗子宮頸癌的疫苗 , 我們現在知道 , 大部分是由人類的大型乳癌所造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現 , 這不是500年前發生的事情 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上我們有了汽車 , 但是我們卻沒意識到我們星球上大部份基因信息組成的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些了不起的工具 , 讓我們可以探索像深度測序的世界 , 這讓我們可以做得更多 , 不僅僅是表面 , 更能從特定物種中看出個別的基因組 , 也能看出整個代謝體 , 那些利用微生物的社群 , 來記錄這些物種的所有基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技術應用在從土壤到皮膚的所有東西上 。
