in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們在定期基礎上做這件事 , 來找出爆發的成因 , 不清楚造成它們的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓各位了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上取了一條娜索 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常做的事 , 來尋找呼吸道病毒 , 例如流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	我們首先會看到的是大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些基因信息 , 我們會看到許多常見的疑問 , 當然 , 很多的人類基因信息 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大部分來自你鼻子裡完全無害的東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到非常、非常令人驚訝的東西 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些資訊時 , 我們會發現你鼻子中大約百分之二十的基因信息並不符合任何我們從未見過的任何東西--沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些研究這種資料的小組 , 我們當中有一些人已經開始稱這些資訊為生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前見過的任何東西 , 這有點像是我們自己的基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子裡有20%的基因信息是許多生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸道 , 高達40%或50%的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對的血液中 , 大約有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質無法被分類 , 不能被輸入或與我們以前見過的任何東西搭配 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為這也許是工藝品 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對比較新 ,
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得越來越準確時 , 我們已經判斷出這些資訊是一種生命形式 , 或至少有一些是生命形式的 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設 , 其實只有在它們的嬰兒體內 , 有非常令人興奮的可能性存在:在這個生命中 , 埋藏在這個基因信息中 , 是尚未被發現的生命跡象 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一連串a、t、c、g時 , 我們可能會發現一個全新的人生階級 , 比如beijerinck , 會從根本上改變我們對生物學本質的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這或許可以讓我們找出一種癌症的成因 , 或是找出我們不熟悉的疫情來源 , 或是在分子生物學中創造出一種新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興能宣佈 , 我和斯坦福大學、加州理工學院、加州理工學院的同事們 , 我們目前正在開始一項計畫 , 探究新形式生命的生物暗物質 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	一百多年前 , 人們沒有意識到病毒 , 我們星球上大部分遺傳信息的生命形式 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚嘆 , 我們可能完全沒意識到我們鼻子底下的一種新生活階級 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能已經把地球上所有的大陸都描繪出來了 , 我們可能發現了外面的所有哺乳類動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的仁慈提供了重要的一課給下一代的探險家 , 像那個來自威斯康辛州貝洛特的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想 , 如果我們說這一教訓 , 它是這樣的:不要假設我們目前認為的全部故事是有的 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	在任何你選擇探索的領域過後 , 去探索黑暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊都有未知 , 他們只是等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇科學家daviddeutsch將理論物理置於後葬人身上來討論一個更急迫的物質:我們物種的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 就是承認我們有一個問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	daviddeutsch在宇宙中的位置 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出一個肢體 , 說些令人驚訝的話 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	所以我會試著這麼做 , 但我想從大家已經知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	第一種 , 事實上 , 是大部分錄音史上所熟知的東西 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境 , 或其它 , 都獨特適合維持我們的進化或創造 , 正如以前所想的 , 以及我們現在的存在 , 最重要的 , 我們的未來生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	如今這個想法有個戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	在太空船之外 , 宇宙是不可思議的 , 而內部是我們所仰賴的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們搞砸了我們的太空船 , 我們還有其他地方要去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件事 , 大家都知道的是 , 和大部分人類歷史所相信的相反 , 事實上 , 人類並不是存在的樞紐 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬•霍金所說 , 我們只是一個在典型的星球表面的化學污垢 , 繞著一個典型的恆星運行 , 它位在典型銀河系的外圍 , 諸如此類 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	第一件大家都知道的事 , 有點像是在說我們處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的服裝等等 , 第二件是說我們處在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是 , 如果你把這兩種深刻的真理視為生活的真理 , 並告訴你的人生決策 , 那麼它們似乎會和彼此產生衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但那並不能阻止他們兩者都是完全錯誤的 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 讓我從第二個例子開始 。 嗯 , 這是典型的地方嗎 ? 嗯 , 我們看看四周 , 看看隨機方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 還有化學污垢 , 這完全不是典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只需要往相同的方向走幾百英里 , 再回頭看 , 你不會看到任何牆面或化學污垢 , 你只能看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你走得更遠 , 你會看到太陽 , 太陽系 , 恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是典型的宇宙 , 因為星星在星系中來臨 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	而宇宙中大部分地方 , 一個典型的地方 , 幾乎沒有任何一個星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	我們再進一步 , 直到我們在星系外面 , 再回頭看 , 沒錯 , 有一個巨大的銀河系 , 有著螺旋手臂躺在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時我們已經從這裡來了十萬光年 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們在宇宙中仍處於一個典型的地方 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 要到達一千倍的星系空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那會是什麼樣子呢 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的地方是什麼樣子的 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在巨大的開銷中 , ted已經安排了高解析度的虛擬實境 , 將星系空間的視野從星系空間看來 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能不能把燈關掉 , 拜託 , 我們能看到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美 , 在星系間太空星系間空間中 , 完全是黑暗的、黑暗的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	黑暗得如此深 , 如果你看著最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星就是要爆炸成超新星 , 而你要直接盯著它 , 當它的光線抵達你時 , 你仍然無法看見甚至是滑稽者 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙有多大和多麼黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星太亮了 , 很棒的一個事件 , 它會在幾光年內殺死你石頭 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系間的空間 , 距離你甚至看不到 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	外面也非常寒冷 , 比絕對零度還要低三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	而且它非常的空氣 。 那裡的真空密度比地球上最好的科技所能創造出來的高一百萬倍 。 所以 , 地球上最好的科技所能創造出來的密度比這個地方高一百萬倍 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這個地方是如此的不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能讓燈光回過來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們怎麼知道這麼遙遠的環境 , 又如此不同 , 如此外星人 , 從我們習慣的任何事物中 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球是我們的環境 , 以我們創造知識的形式 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 這是什麼意思呢 ? 嗯 , 比我們剛才說的更遠--我是說 , 用望遠鏡--你會看到看起來像星星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 石器 」 。 石器原本指的是量子論物體 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	也就是說 , 看起來有點像星星的東西 。 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	而我們知道它們是幾十億年前的樣子 , 數十億光年之遙 , 星系中心的物質會倒塌 , 朝向一個超大質量黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後強烈的磁場引導了那重力崩塌的一些能量 。 還有一些物質 , 回到極大的噴射流形式 , 用光線照亮了幾兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理現象幾乎不像噴射機的物理現象 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法在其中一個噴射機中存活下來 。 語言在試圖描述噴射機中會是什麼樣子 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這會有點像體驗超新星爆炸 , 但在時間點與數百萬年間 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 這噴射機在幾十億年後發生了 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 模型 , 並預測 , 並解釋 , 最重要的是 , 你的參考點在現實中發生了什麼 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個實體系統 , 大腦 , 包含另一個量子的準確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是它的超面部影像 , 雖然它也包含這樣 , 還有一個解釋性的模型 , 體現出相同的數學關係和相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 信仰與另一種結構相似 , 那就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	那個實體物體 , 儘可能和彼此不一樣 , 不論如何體現出相同的數學和因果結構 , 隨時間來做 , 都越來越多 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以我們是一個不一樣的化學污垢 。 這個化學污垢具有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含了不斷增加的精確度 , 所有事物的結構 。 這個地方 , 不是宇宙中的其他地方 , 它的一個樞紐 , 包含了整個物理世界的結構和因果關係 。 到目前為止 , 物理定律不足以讓這個現象發生 , 甚至被強化 , 是物理世界中最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	現在 , 太陽系和我們的環境 , 如何在我們取得這個與宇宙其餘的特殊關係中 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬.霍金的印象中有一件事是真的 , 這是真的 , 但卻是錯誤的強調 。 其中的一件事是 , 沒有任何特殊的物理現象 。 沒有特殊的干擾 , 沒有奇蹟 , 涉及的奇蹟 。 這只是我們這裡有三樣東西的豐富性 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理的形式 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要一台電腦--沒有任何物質的製造方式 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能源來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 讓媒體能夠有效地實現我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三點 , 較不具體 , 但對開放性創造知識、解釋的開放性 , 卻是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛好開始進行測試 , 比方說 , 牛頓的重力定律大約在300年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但是我們以前所做的證據已經落在地球的每平方公尺上 , 在那之前數十億年 , 將會持續落在幾十億年之後 。 其他科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 發現所有科學中最基本的真理 , 就在於地球上發生 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的位置充滿了證據 , 同時也帶著物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三項準備是開放式知識的創造 , 是他們最低可能的供應 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說 , 它是空的 , 它是冷的 , 外面是暗的 。 還是它 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	其實 , 這只是另一個狹隘的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個在星系間空間的立方體 , 和我們的家一樣大的尺寸 , 太陽系 。 現在這個立方體是人類的標準非常空的 , 但這仍然意味著它包含了超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造一座自助的太空站 , 那裡有一群科學家 , 致力於創造一個開放式的知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 遠遠超越了科技 , 來收集來自星系間空間的氫氣 , 將其形成成其他元素之類的 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在可理解的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西不被物理定律所禁止 , 那麼 , 什麼可能讓我們不去做 , 除了知道怎麼做 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是知識的問題 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們可以自動進行能源供應 , 因為轉變將是核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 再一次 , 人類的感官是暗的 。 但是你只需要拿一個望遠鏡 , 即便是今天的一個設計 , 向外看 , 你會看到我們從這裡看到的同一個星系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更強大的望遠鏡 , 你就能看到恆星 , 行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你將能夠進行天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在當地你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理學 , 還有化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	最困難的科學可能是生物學領域的旅行 , 因為要幾億年才能到達最近的生命星球 , 回到最近的星球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但我必須告訴各位 , 很抱歉 , 理查但我從來沒有太像生物學領域旅行過 , 我想我們每隔幾億年就只能用一個 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以 , 事實上 , 星系間空間確實包含了開放知識的所有前提 。 任何在宇宙中的任何一個立方體 , 都可能變成和我們一樣的樞紐 , 假如我們知道該如何做的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以我們不是在一個獨特的福利地方 ,
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間空間有能力創造出一個開放式的解釋流 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境都如此 。 這就是地球 。 所以 , 這是個受污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而有限的因素 , 在這裡和這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為它們很豐富 , 但知識 , 很稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個宇宙知識基礎的觀點也許和我認為應該讓我們覺得非常特別 。 但這也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若沒有需要的特定知識 , 能夠生存下去面對宇宙的挑戰 , 我們就不會存活下來 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要幾光年之外的超新星 , 我們就要死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁瑞斯最近寫了一本書 , 內容是關於我們對於各種事物的脆弱性 , 從天體物理 , 到科學實驗都出了錯 , 最重要的是對大規模毀滅性武器的恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為 , 文明在這個世紀僅有50%的存活機會 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他在會議後會談到這點
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	現在我不認為這個機率是正確的分類來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我也同意他這樣做 。 我們可以生存下去 , 我們無法生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但它不依賴機會 , 而是我們是否在時間內創造出相關知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險並不是前所未有的 。 物種隨時都滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明就結束了 。 絕大多數物種和所有曾經存在過的文明都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想要成為例外 , 那麼 , 邏輯上 , 我們唯一的希望就是要用一個區別我們物種的特徵 , 以及我們的文明 , 取名為 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新解釋的能力 , 新知識成為存在的樞紐 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我把它應用到目前的爭議中 , 不是因為我想要倡導任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是用來說明我所指的 。
and the controversy is global warming .	而爭議是全球暖化
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	現在 , 我是物理學家 , 但我不是正確的物理學家 。 不論是全球暖化 , 我都只是個懶惰 。 對於層級人來說 , 理性的一件事 , 就是認真看待前衛的科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 已經太遲到可以避免一場災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為 , 如果說我們當下最好的選項是預防二氧化碳排放 , 像是京都議定書 , 它的限制在經濟活動上的限制 , 以及它的巨大成本 , 數千億美元或不論是什麼 , 那那已經是任何合理的措施所造成的災難 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	而那些被倡導的行動 , 甚至還沒被追求去解決問題 , 僅僅只是稍微延伸它 。 所以它已經太遲了 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它了 , 從任何人意識到危險之前就已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	大概在1970年代已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放即將促進一個新的冰河時期 , 數十億人會死亡 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這教訓對我來說很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼它沒有公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們不能永遠知道 。 當我們知道一場即將發生的災難 , 以及如何以低於災難本身的成本來解決這個問題 , 那麼就不會有太多的爭論 , 真的 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防準則 , 可以避免我們尚未預見的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一大堆問題 , 不僅是問題的一部分 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	事實是 , 一盎司的預防等於一磅的治癒 , 但只有在我們知道要預防什麼 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你曾在鼻子上打過 , 那麼醫學的科學就不會一致教你如何避免拳頭 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學停止尋求解藥 , 只專注在預防上 , 那它也不會達到任何目標 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	在當下 , 世界正在進行計劃迫使氣體排放減量 , 不計代價 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要用計劃來降低溫度 , 用計劃在更高的溫度生活 , 不需要任何成本 , 但有效率和便宜 。 還有一些這樣的計劃存在 , 例如太空中的鏡子群來反射陽光 , 並鼓勵水猿生物吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	在當下 , 這些東西是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類努力去面對這個問題的中心 , 或是一般性的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	有了我們還沒意識到的問題 , 能放對的能力 , 不是無限避免的好運 , 是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 還有生存的能力 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	所以拿兩個石板 , 然後雕刻在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一個 , 雕刻: 「 問題是解決之道 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一塊雕刻: 「 問題是必然的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個掙扎的國家如何打破貧窮 , 如果被困在一個不好的規則系統中 ? 經濟學家保羅•羅默揭露出一個大膽的想法: 「 特許城市 」 , 城市規模的行政區被一個國家聯盟所控制 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	企業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅•羅默的激進想法:特許城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了非常迷人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的路燈下做功課 , 因為家裡沒有電 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	現在 , 我還沒遇到這些特別的學生 , 但我遇到了像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉例來說 , 綠色上衣的那件
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也給他一個名字:尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我敢打賭nelson有一個手機
so here is the puzzle .	這裡的謎題是
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森能取得尖端科技 , 例如手機 , 但無法取得一百歲的科技 , 來供電給家中產生的電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	一句話 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以防止這種雙贏的解決方案 , 當人們能把新科技帶進來 , 讓它們成為像納爾遜這樣的人 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這間國家的電力公司在一條規則下運作 , 說它必須以非常低的價格來銷售電力 , 事實上 , 一個價格低到每一單位都要賣 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 它沒有資源 , 也沒有獎勵 , 可以接上許多其他用戶 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想改變這個規則
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到可以有不同的規則規則 , 企業賺取小額利潤的規則 , 所以他們有獎勵去簽訂更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這就是手機公司的那種規則 , 尼爾森從操作部門購買了他的電話 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看過那些規則如何運作良好
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變用電費的規則 , 但卻跑進一場抗議活動 , 來自商業和消費者想要保存既有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他陷入了規則 , 阻止他讓雙贏解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森在街燈下陷入研究 ,
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是試著找出我們能改變規則的方法 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	是否有一些規則我們可以為改變規則發展 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想主張 , 有一個普遍的抽象洞見 , 可以讓我們做出實用的洞見 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給人們更多的選擇 , 以及更多的選擇 , 給予許多國家的領導人 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 要呈現這兩者之間的反對是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能會想要給予領導人的那種選擇 , 像給予總統在電力上提高價格的選擇 , 奪走人們想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能選擇繼續消費補助電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以 , 如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到給兩者更多選擇的方法 , 那就給了我們一組改變規則 , 讓我們脫離陷阱的規則 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	現在 , nelson也能上網
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說如果你想看到規則的傷害效果 , 規則能讓人們保持在黑暗中 , 看看地球上太空總署的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別檢查亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在這裡 , 在外線 , 這就像一個黑洞 , 和它的鄰居相比 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝地發現北韓的規則保持在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但很重要的是 , 要意識到北韓和南韓始於一模一樣的規則 , 在法律和法規的感覺中 , 一開始是一模一樣的規則 , 但也在更深層的層面上 , 了解、規範、文化、價值觀和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做了選擇 , 導致他們有非常多樣化的規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們人類可以改變我們用的規則 , 來和彼此互動 , 做得更好 , 或更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個地區 , 加勒比海
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 在外線這裡 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 相較於它的鄰居 , 多明尼加共和國 , 大約有數量相同的居民 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家都是黑暗的 , 相較於波多黎各 , 居民的數量有一半是海地或多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們 , 規則可能很糟 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只是規則不好 , 因為政府太強壯和壓迫 , 就像北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要用好的規則來創造環境 , 我們就不能直接撕下來 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須找到建設的方法 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國大大展現出與規則合作的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到這張圖表的開端 , 中國是世界高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國有先驅技術如鋼、印刷、槍械 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國從來沒有採用過 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則 , 鼓勵那些想法的傳播 , 一個能鼓勵傳播出去的利潤動機 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用規則 , 讓創新慢下來 , 把中國從世界其他地方切斷 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界其他國家的創新 , 在發展更新科技的意義上 , 同時也發展出更新的規則 , 中國也從那些進步中被切斷 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	那裡的收入持續停滯 , 隨著它在世界其他地方放大 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表更近期的資料
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它繪製了收入 , 中國的平均收入 , 佔了美國平均收入的比例 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50年代和60年代 , 你可以看到它的覆蓋率大約是3% 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但到了70年代末期 , 發生了改變 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國的成長開始迅速趕上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你在晚上回到地圖上 , 就能得到一個線索 , 引導中國規則的戲劇性改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的點 , 在這裡可以看到線的邊緣 , 就是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀 , 大部分的規則下運作 , 比起當時工作市場經濟的其他大陸規則 , 大部份的中國規則所規範 , 並由英國主導 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個有數百萬人可以去的地方 , 來自大陸 , 開始做縫紉衫的工作 , 製作玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了增加收入的過程 , 增加的技能 , 導致那裡的成長非常快速 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是領導人 , 像鄧小平能複製的模式 , 當他們決定將所有大陸移到市場模式時 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到 , 對他的人民提供選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫中國的每個人立即轉移到市場模式 , 他們通過創造一些可以做到的特殊區塊 , 在某種意義上 , 英國所做的是:讓有機會和市場規則合作 , 帶給那些想在裡面採購的人 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港附近創建了四個特別的經濟區:中國地區可以來上班 , 都市成長得很快 ; 還有外交公司可以進來製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個地區有一個叫做深圳的城市
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那座城市裡 , 有一個台灣公司 , 讓你們當中許多人擁有的iphone , 他們用從搬到深圳的中國勞工製作 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特區之後 , 有14個海岸線 , 都是以同樣的觀點開放的 , 最終在這些人們可以選擇進去的地方展現出成功 , 他們會因為他們提供的優勢而被封鎖 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	證實了成功 , 導致了一種共識 , 能向整個經濟體邁進市場模式 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在中國的例子讓我們看到了幾點
one is: preserve choices for people .	一是:保留人們的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	二:在正確的尺度上運作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變村落裡的規則 , 你可以做到 , 但村落太小了 , 要是你有好幾百萬人在好的規則下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國內的規則 , 你就不能給一些人一個機會去抓住 , 看看事情的結果如何 , 並讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給了你這個機會 , 創造新的地方 , 有了人們可以選擇的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們大到足以獲得我們所能擁有的所有利益 , 只要有數百萬人在好的規則下一起工作 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 提案是我們對某樣東西的概念 , 叫做 「 特許城市 」 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個特定規則開始 , 明確指定所有規則 , 來吸引那些我們需要建造城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 他們會建立基礎建設──電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引公司 , 誰會先到那兒去雇用那些先搬到那兒去的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你會需要吸引家庭 , 那些將來會永久生活的居民 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 得到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了那張圖 , 人們會搬到那裏去 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造
and we can scale this model .	而我們可以擴大這個模型
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一而再、再而三地
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	為了讓它運作 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些在憲章中捕捉到的
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這真的是建立在模型中 , 如果我們能夠在不被居住的土地上建立城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從不居住的領土開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以在新憲章中過來 , 但沒有人被迫活下去 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	我們最需要的就是領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要的領導者 , 我們需要允許國與國之間合作的潛力:國與國之間的合作關係 , 實際上 , 中國和英國合作的方式 , 首先建立一個小規模的市場模式 , 接著擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 無意間 , 透過它在香港的行動 , 減少世界貧窮的程度 , 比上個世紀所有援助計畫還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以 , 如果我們允許這類夥伴關係再次複製 , 我們就能讓這類的益處在世界各地擴大 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到負責任的刪除 , 從一個國家到另一個國家的控制權 , 來掌握某些特定的行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我這麼說的時候 , 有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	並非如此 。 但很重要的是要意識到當我們開始思考這些事情時所產生的那種情緒 , 能夠以一種方式 , 讓我們能拉回來 , 能夠關掉我們的能力 , 以及我們想要探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義的壞處在於 , 在我們的一些援助計畫中 , 遺憾的壞處在於 , 它涉及了強制和縮寫的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式都是關於選擇 , 對於領導人 , 和那些會住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	而且 , 選擇是對強制和衰退的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	我們來談談如何在練習中演出 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們來一個特別的領袖 , 拉爾•卡斯楚 , 他是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	他一定有機會幫古巴小提琴做些什麼 , 但他在古巴沒有香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他的確有一點點亮 , 在南方有很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在瓜地亞摩灣附近有一個區塊 , 一個條約給了美國行政區的一塊地 , 一塊大約是曼哈頓兩倍大的土地 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚前往加拿大總理說: 「 聽著 , 伊恩克斯有一個糟糕的pr問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不 , 加拿大 , 接下去 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特別的行政區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	允許一個新城市在上面建設
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓附近的香港
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些公民也會搬進那座城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會回頭 。 但這會是將現代經濟和現代世界連結到我的國家的大門 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這個模式還能在哪裡試驗 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人完全把一個特區的概念拿來當作一個規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	改變規則的規則
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	這是創造新規則的方法 , 讓民眾不需要強制 , 而強制的反對者也能強迫 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以向長期投資者做出更有信心的承諾 , 那種將來建造港口、建造道路的投資者 , 在新城市中 , 他們可以做出更有信心的承諾 , 只要他們和一個夥伴國家一起做 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許在某些安排中 , 有點像是escrow帳戶 , 你把土地放在escrow帳戶裡 , 另一半國家為此負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲也有許多土地 , 在那裡 , 新城市可以建造 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我沿著海岸飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	這裡有巨大的延伸土地 , 像這片土地 , 那裡有數億人可以居住 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	如果我們歸納出這點 , 想想看 , 不僅僅只有一、兩個特定地點 , 還有數十個城市 , 會協助創造出數億人的地方 , 也許數十億人會搬到上個世紀的城市 , 那裡有足夠的土地給他們嗎 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在整個世界 , 如果我們晚上看燈 , 其中一個誤導的是 , 視覺上 , 它看起來世界上大部分已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我來說明為什麼那是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以這代表所有的土地為例
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	轉變成一個正方形 , 代表地球上所有可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經被三十億人口居住的城市佔據的土地
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點移到長方形的底部 , 你可以看到 , 現存的三十億城市居民只佔地球上可耕地的三成 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想為另外十億人建造城市 , 他們就會像這樣 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們會從可耕地的3%降到4% 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們大大降低地球上的人類足跡 , 藉由建造更多人可以移動的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市被好的規則所統治 , 它們可以是人們安全的城市 , 不受犯罪、安全 , 不受到疾病和不良衛生 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會得到一份工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們可以得到像電一樣基本的功用 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以得到教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要開始建造第一座特許城市 , 要做的是什麼 , 讓我們再建造更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	會有助於有了手冊
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授能做的是寫一些細節 , 可能會進入這個手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們運行城市 , 出去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者在野外出去
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考一些問題 , 例如 , 假設這不僅僅是加拿大在處理 「 拉爾•卡斯楚 」 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西是參與者 , 也是西班牙人 , 也許古巴人也想成為四向合作的夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要怎麼寫條約才能做到 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	對此有較少的先例 , 但那很容易就能實現 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何融資 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	原來新加坡和香港是城市 , 在他們開始時所擁有的土地價值上 , 造成了巨大的增加 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用土地的價值來支付像警察、法庭等的東西 , 但學校系統和醫療系統也一樣 , 這讓這一個更有吸引力的地方居住 , 讓這地方的人有更高的收入 , 這點不小心 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 人們協助建構這個區塊的誘因 , 並設立基本規則 , 往正確的方向前進 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有很多類似的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們怎麼會有低成本和負擔得起的人在第一份工作中工作 , 組裝類似iphone的東西 , 但讓那些建築物有效率 , 並確保它們是安全的 , 所以它們不會在地震或颶風中墜落 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節可以被解決 , 但那些已經開始追求這些事情的人 , 已經知道沒有道路 , 沒有障礙 , 沒有任何阻礙 , 除了想像的失敗之外 , 還會讓我們無法實現真正的全球雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片做結論 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能如此良好 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享想法 , 當他們發現它們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	這不像稀少的物品 , 分享的意思是我們每人都能得到的更少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一種想法:規則管理我們如何與彼此互動 ; 規則像是 , 讓我們有一個稅制 , 支持一項研究大學 , 免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一套系統 , 我們擁有一塊地 , 在政府辦公室註冊 , 讓人們可以承受大學知識份子 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們可以繼續創新在我們規則的空間上尤其是創新在我們想出改變規則的規則上所以我們不會被困在不好的規則上那麼我們就可以繼續前進 , 真正地讓世界變得更好所以像nelson和他的朋友不用再在街燈下學習謝謝
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因組學先鋒克萊格•凡特從他的史詩圓圓形探險中休息了一會 , 探討了數以百萬計的基因 , 他的團隊發現到目前為止 , 目前為止 , 探測海洋生物多樣性的地圖 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生態圈、生物科技、企業家、遺傳學、發明、海洋、科學、科技、科技 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	dna和海上的克萊格•凡特
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 我被幾個人問到我對於衰老辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我明白樂觀主義者極度過於悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我18分鐘內 , 我要告訴各位的是我們如何從閱讀遺傳密碼轉換到開始寫程式碼的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅在10年前的這個月我們發表了第一批自由生命體的有機體的序列那就是嗜血桿菌的流感
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這花了13年的基因組計劃 , 降到四個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八個小時內完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去的十年裡 , 大量的基因組加起來:大部分的人類病原體 , 幾種植物 , 幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳類 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十多年前 , 思維的基因組學在今年年底 , 我們可能在三到五個基因組定序之間有基因組 , 數百個基因組 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登和貝蒂.摩爾基金會得到一個資助 , 到今年130個基因組定序 , 作為一個來自環境生物的副產品 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀遺傳密碼的速率已經改變了
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但 , 如我們所見 , 外面有什麼 , 我們幾乎沒有抓到這個星球上可取得的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分的人都沒有意識到 , 因為他們是看不見的 , 但微生物組成大約地球一半的生物量 , 而所有的動物只會組成大約所有生物量的1/3 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是在牛津的人們不太常做的事 , 但如果你曾經到海裡 , 吞下一口海水 , 請記住 , 每一毫升都有大約一百萬個細菌 , 以及一千萬種病毒的順序 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	不到5000個微生物種類在兩年前就已經被特徵化了 , 所以我們決定要為此做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了不久的二次探險 , 和很棒的海洋探險隊一樣 , 每200英里就要採樣海洋 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始進行我們的測試計畫 , 然後搬到哈利法克斯 , 向美國東岸工作 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿越加拉帕戈斯 , 橫越太平洋 , 我們現在正處在印度洋的路上 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的責任 , 我們在帆船上做這件事 , 有一部分可以協助讓年輕人興奮地進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只拿海水來過濾 , 用不同的濾網來收集不同的大小生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們每24小時就能排序出一億個字母基因密碼 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	藉由這麼做 , 我們做了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 有人認為在我們眼中所看到的視覺色素只有一到兩種有機體在環境中有著相同的色素
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎全世界上層的海洋都有這些相同的感光受器 , 並將陽光當作它們的能量和溝通來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地點 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了一百三十萬個新基因 , 和多達五萬個新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在把這張圖延伸到空中 , 用的是來自sloan基金會的補助金 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量有多少病毒和細菌每天都呼吸進去 , 特別是在飛機上或關閉禮堂上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們過濾了一些簡單的儀器 ; 我們收集了十億個微生物的數量 , 從僅僅一天在紐約市的一棟建築物上過濾出來 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	而我們正處於目前的定序過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	只要在數據收集面上 , 只要我們在加拉帕戈斯的位置 , 我們就會發現 , 幾乎每200英里 , 我們在海洋樣本中看到極大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些在邏輯上是有道理的 , 就不同的溫度而言 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 根據溫度的紅色 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現溫暖的樣本和冷水樣本之間有很大的差異 , 以豐富的物種來說 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另外一個讓我們相當驚訝的是這些光受體偵測不同的波長 , 我們可以根據它們的氨基酸序列來預測這個現象 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	而這些從地區到地區都有極大的影響 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外地 , 在深海中 , 大部分是藍色的 , 照片接收器傾向於看到藍色光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有很多葉綠素時 , 他們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們甚至更有可能會朝紅外線和紫外線前進 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	只是為了評估我們的基因重複是什麼 , 我們把所有的資料組合起來 , 包括我們所有的資料 , 遠離探險的資料 , 它們代表地球上超過一半的基因資料 , 總共有兩千九百萬個基因資料 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著將這些放入基因家庭 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們是否只是發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是發現新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但每個我們在環境中採取的新樣本 , 都以線性的方式增加到這些新家庭 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	因此 , 我們正處於發現基本基因、組成和生命的最早階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看著所謂的演化樹 , 我們就在右上角和動物在一起 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在那些大約2千9百萬個基因中 , 我們只有大約2萬4千個基因組 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物都聚集在一起 , 我們可能共有不到三萬隻 , 也許還有十幾千個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我認為這些基因現在不僅僅是演化的設計元素
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	而我們認為在一個基因中心的觀點也許回到理查德•道金斯的想法 , 比以基因為中心的觀點 , 這和這些基因組成的組成不同 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力 , 已經改變了某種程度上 , dna定序的速度在過去十年或兩年間 , 越來越快 , 非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們對合成基因組學的第一個想法是當我們在1995年將第二個基因組定序後 , 而那是從mycoasma生殖器中來的 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有非常棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我心我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	大象有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們簡單地問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 另一個500 , 有沒有一個更小的基因可以比一個最小的操作系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始進行轉化突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	運輸只是遺傳密碼中隨機插入的小片段dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果他們插入基因的中間 , 就會干擾它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以 , 我們做了一張地圖 , 圖上可以將轉移插入的所有基因 , 我們稱之為 「 無證基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但結果發現 , 環境對此非常重要 , 你只能根據環境中的東西來定義一個必要或沒有證據的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用一個更直接的智力方法 , 用13個相關有機體的基因組 , 我們試著比較所有這些 , 看看它們有什麼共通點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們得到了這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現只有173個基因共通點 , 到達了13個有機體 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	水池擴大了一點 , 如果我們忽略了一個細胞寄生蟲 ; 當我們觀察核心組成的基因時 , 它擴大了更多 , 大約是310左右 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴大或收縮基因組 , 取決於你這裡的觀點 , 到大約300到400個基因 , 從500個最小的基因組 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	唯一能證明這些想法的方法是用人工染色體和那些基因在裡面的人工染色體 , 我們必須在以鑄造為基礎的時尚中這麼做 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現在大片中合成精確的dna是極其困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hamsmith和clydehutchison , 我的同事開發出了一個令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能夠合成一個5000個核心對立病毒 , 在只有2個週期中 , 它是100%精確的 , 在它的序列和生物學方面 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個相當振奮人心的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna , 注入細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始驅動病毒粒子的生產 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成病毒--一種小兒麻痺病毒--已經一年製造了--但它只有一個十分之一的活躍性--花了三年的時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的結構結構的漫畫 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是軟體目前建造自己的硬體的案例 , 那就是我們和生物學有關係的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上開始關心生物戰事 , 我在參議院委員會之前就有最近的證據 , 還有一個特別的委員會 , 美國政府設立了來審查這個領域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	而我認為 , 保持現實是很重要的 , 與人們的想像力相反 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 現今任何已定序的病毒都可以做出
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上就嚇壞了關於伊波拉或天花的事物 , 但這個生物體的dna並不是傳染性的 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人製造天花基因組 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正關心安全部門有的真正關心的是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 致力於創造生物戰事代理人 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那個研究真的被消滅掉了 , 在未來應該有非常少的活動來製造設計師病毒 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為 , 單細胞生物在兩年內可能
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能在十年內 , 那些我們所擁有的電子細胞 , 是可能的 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在製造了好幾十種不同的建構 , 因為我們可以將種子和進入這種人工染色體的基因改造 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 如何把所有其他人
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 接著我們有了一個全體的重組系統 , 將這些組合成一條染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體衍生出來的 , deinoccusradiodurans , 它可以承受三百萬個輻射 , 且不會被殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在這個放射線爆裂後 , 它會在大約12到24小時內重新組合成它的染色體 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上無所不在 , 可能存在於外太空 , 由於我們在那兒的旅行 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是個玻璃製片 , 經過約50萬雷射之後 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 微生物坐在底部變得更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是一張實際發生的圖片:這張圖的上方顯示了一百七十萬個輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體真的會被打破 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna在24小時後會自動重組 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	這真的很驚人 , 這些生物體能做到 , 我們可能有數千個 , 如果不是數萬個 , 在這個星球上有能力做到的不同物種 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組合後 , 第一步只是移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	因此我們認為合成細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 也為了期待環境和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們定序的第三個有機體 , 甲烷occusjannaschii , 它活在沸騰的水溫中 ; 它的能源來源是氫 , 它所有的碳都來自於它從環境中捕捉到的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 數以千計的不同生物 , 活在二氧化碳之外 , 可以捕捉到這些 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其從石油取得合成程序的碳 , 我們有機會使用碳 , 從大氣中捕捉它 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物住在一氧化碳之外 , 我們用作為減少水分的力量 , 來產生氫氣和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有許多途徑可以被工程化代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦在挪威有一項重大計畫 , 可以捕捉並將氣體場的甲烷轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在短短的一段時間內 , 我認為將會有一個新領域 , 叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為 , 有了這些新的合成能力 , 這些廣大的基因陣列重組 , 以及同源基因重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 一天可能製造出一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同所有的生物 , 你透過篩選 , 不論你是在篩選氫產量 , 或是化學產量 , 或只是可見性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若要了解這些基因的作用會很好 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用 , 從陽光中直接產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節 , 我們有一個氧氣敏感的氫化物 , 我們認為將完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合纖維素 , 將複雜糖分解成簡單的糖和發酵在同細胞中 , 以產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	製藥生產已經在主要實驗室使用微生物的方式下降 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物的化學性質是比我們最好的化學家能生產的還要複雜的數量級 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能源的來源 , 環境的補救 , 或許還能取代石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究來做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們延遲了1999年的實驗開始 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審查 , 到我們是否該嘗試製造一個人工物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是一項非常奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖都把他們的經文當作法律書籍 , 他們找不到任何禁止製造生命的東西 , 所以這也沒問題 。 唯一的終極顧慮就是生物戰事的面向 , 但給了我們前面這些實驗 , 為我們開始做這些實驗 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在 , sloan基金會剛剛資助一個多元化的機構研究 , 找出對社會的風險和利益是什麼 , 以及科學團隊的規則 , 例如我自己在這個領域應該使用的規則 , 我們正試著在前進時設定好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的議題
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是非常簡單的議題 , 我們能否設計一些東西來生產乾淨能源 , 或許能革新發展中國家能做些什麼 , 並透過各種簡單的過程提供 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家philipzimbardo說 , 快樂和成功是根深蒂固的 , 我們大部分人都忽略了:我們向過去、現在和未來邁進的方式 。 他建議我們用時間校正我們的出發點 , 來改善我們的生活 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、幸福、思想、心理、心理、科學、科學 。
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo開出一個健康的準確度 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些點子關於時間的秘密力量 , 在很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好 , 開始時鐘拜託 。 30秒鐘的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 , 安頓下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	大約是時間 。 結束序列 。 拿一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10 , 9 , 7 , 6 , 5 , 4 , 3 , 2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利普•辛巴多:咱們來談談亞當的誘惑 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來亞當 , 別這麼想好好 , 先說一下 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 。 別棄伊娃 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 ,
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 。 一口 , 地獄是什麼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是誘惑 。 一切都是為了產出 , 抗拒 , 是的 , 不 , 現在 , 晚點 , 衝動 , 反思 , 目前的焦點和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾的美德會落入當下的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	在青少年時期 , 一直在婚姻中謝謝喬治布希大部份 , 60% , 導致性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部分都沒有使用節育法 。
so much for promises .	這麼多的承諾
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓四歲小孩誘惑 , 給他們一個治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然是付錢的 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 等一下 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	會發生的是三分之二的孩子會給予誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 , 其他人 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 晚點再延遲 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	waltermychel , 我在史丹佛的同事 , 14年後回去 , 試著去發現那些孩子的不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多方面 , 反抗和孩子的孩子之間 , 有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些抗拒分數250分的孩子 , 坐著就更高 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這相當巨大 。 這就像一整組不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有遇到那麼多麻煩 , 他們是更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們自信和堅決 。 至今 , 對我來說 , 關鍵在於你 , 他們是未來的焦點 , 而不是當下的焦點 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間觀點是研究個人、我們所有人 , 將你人類經驗的流動分成時間區或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而你會自動、無意識地做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	他們在文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育水平之間的差異 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 他們可以變得有偏見 , 因為你學會過度使用它們 , 用到其他人身上 。
what determines any decision you make ?	什麼決定了你做的決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你要做一個決定 , 你要做一個動作 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在立即的情況下 , 別人在做什麼 , 以及你感受到什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們在那種形式中做出決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 目前為止 」 , 因為他們的焦點就是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是在說 「 我過去經歷過的這種情況是什麼樣的 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定是建立在過去的記憶上 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們打算把那些人稱為 「 過去證書 」 , 因為他們把焦點放在 「 是什麼 」 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 也不是現在 , 只關乎未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是有關預期的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們要稱呼他們為 「 未來因素 」 。 他們的焦點是在將來會是什麼 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想辯論 , 時間觀的悖論 , 是影響你所做的每一決定 , 你完全沒意識到的事 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	意思是 , 這種程度你有偏見的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六種 。 有兩種方式可以呈現 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式被放牧 , 有兩種方式可以成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在 「 正面 」 或 「 負面 」 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是現代主義的 , 取名為你把焦點放在生活的喜悅上 , 或是當代人──這並不重要 , 你的人生被控制了 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來的、設定目標的 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者是超然的未來:名字 , 生命始於死後 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出心理靈活性 , 轉換時間的觀點 , 取決於局勢的要求 , 這就是你必須學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 最佳時空檔是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	積極的高度 , 未來的高度 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	以及對現況主義的調適 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	永遠低於過去的負面和現況主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的顳葉混合體是你從過去的過度積極帶給你的根源 。 你連結你的家人、身份 , 和你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來得到的是翅膀 , 到翱翔到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的享樂主義得到的就是能量 , 探索自己、位置、人、感性 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何時間的觀點都有比正面的負面多
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來為成功犧牲了什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 。 他們犧牲朋友時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲好玩的時間 。 他們犧牲了個人的侮辱 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了嗜好 , 犧牲了睡眠 。 所以這會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	而他們為工作、成就和控制而生活 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我敢肯定和一些tedster產生共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這對我有共鳴 。 我成長於南布朗克斯貧民區一個貧窮的孩子 , 一個住在過去和現在的西尼亞家庭 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我身為一個前往頂端的人 , 做這些犧牲的人 , 因為老師介入了 , 讓我有了未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等到你要拿到兩顆 , 直到我學會取得平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了現代主義 , 我把焦點加到 「 過度積極 」 , 所以 , 在76歲時 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們把這個應用在許多世界的問題上:改變輟學的比率 , 結合成癮 , 增強青少年健康 , 用時間的比喻 , 治好ptsd , 取得奇蹟的治療方法 , 促進永續性和保育 , 減少身體復健的比率 , 增加了50% , 改變了自殺恐怖分子的申請 , 並將家庭衝突改造成時間軸 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說一句話:許多生命的謎題都可以透過了解你的時間觀點和其他人的解答 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果真的很深奧 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	在100年內 , 有多少頭條會很重要 ? 1000年 ? kirkcitron的 「 長新聞 」 計畫收集了不只重要的故事 , 還會讓數十年來的新聞出現 。 在ted2010年 , 他發起了近期的頭條 , 用潛力來形塑我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:而現在 , 真正的新聞
we are drowning in news .	我們在新聞中溺死 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	單單單單讓路人每年發佈350萬則新聞 。
that's just one source .	那只是一個來源 。
